古今图书集成医部全录卷三百二十一

情志门

　　　　黄帝素问

　　　　　阴阳应象大论

　　心在声为笑，在变动为忧，在志为喜。喜伤心，恐胜喜。　　【注　心志喜，故发声为笑。心独无俞，故变动在志，心气并于肺则忧。在志为喜，此心中和乐也。过于喜则心志自伤。恐胜喜者，恐为肾志，水胜火也。】　　肝在声为呼，在变动为握，在志为怒，怒伤肝，悲胜怒。　　 【注　肝者将军之官，故在志为怒，而发声为叫呼也。怒伤肝者，用志太过，则反伤其体矣。悲胜怒者，悲为肺志，以情胜情也。】　　脾在声为歌，在变动为哕，在志为思。思伤脾，怒胜思。[1p]

Comprehensive Collection of Ancient and Modern Books, Volume 321

On Emotions and Will

Huangdi's Suwen

On the Great Discussion of Yin and Yang Correspondences

The heart expresses joy through laughter, reacts to change with worry, and embodies will with happiness. Excessive joy harms the heart, while fear overcomes joy. [Note: Joy from the heart leads to laughter. When the heart is unimpeded, it reacts to change with will; when heart energy converges in the lungs, it causes worry. Happiness embodies harmony and joy in the heart. Excessive joy can injure the heart’s will. When fear overcomes joy, it refers to the will of the kidneys, as water overcomes fire.] The liver expresses anger through shouting, reacts to change with grasping, and embodies will with fury. Anger harms the liver, while sorrow overcomes anger. [Note: The liver, as the general's office, is thus associated with anger, expressed through shouting. Anger injures the liver when will becomes excessive, harming the body in turn. Sorrow overcomes anger because sorrow relates to the lungs, illustrating emotion overcoming emotion.] The spleen expresses thoughts through singing, reacts to change with hiccups, and embodies will with contemplation. Contemplation harms the spleen, while anger overcomes contemplation.[1p]

　　 【注　脾主运用，故其志在思，发声为歌也。思伤脾者，用志则伤气，气伤则脏伤也。怒为肝志，故能胜思。】　　肺在声为哭，在变动为咳，在志为忧。忧伤肺，喜胜忧。　　 【注　肺志在悲，故发声为哭。脏气变动，则及于喉而为咳也。若精气并于肺则忧。忧伤肺者，过则损也。喜则气散，故能胜忧。】　　肾在声为呻，在变动为栗，在志为恐。恐伤肾，思胜恐。　　 【注　肾气在下，故声欲太息而呻出之。肾藏志而为作强之官，故虑事而时怀恐怖也。恐伤肾者，恐惧而不解则伤精也。思虑深则处事详，故胜恐。】[2p]

The spleen governs movement, thus its intention is in thought, and its expression is as song. Excessive thinking harms the spleen; using intention can then harm qi, and if qi is harmed, the organs are also affected. Anger is related to the liver's intention, hence it can overcome thought.

The lungs express sound as crying, move as coughing, and their intention is worry. Worry harms the lungs, while joy overcomes worry. The intention of the lungs is sorrow, therefore its expression is crying. When lung qi moves, it reaches the throat and causes coughing. When essence and qi unify in the lungs, it leads to worry. Worry harms the lungs; excessive worry causes damage. Joy disperses qi, thus it can overcome worry.

The kidneys express sound as moaning, move as shivering, and their intention is fear. Fear harms the kidneys, while thought overcomes fear. Kidney qi is deep, thus the sound emerges as a deep sigh or moan. The kidneys store intention and act as a strong official, hence they often harbor fears concerning matters. Fear harms the kidneys; if one is fearful and unable to resolve it, it can damage the essence. Deep thought allows for detailed action, which can therefore overcome fear.[2p]

　　　　　灵兰秘典论

　　膻中者，臣使之官，喜乐出焉。
　　 【注　膻中者，心主之宫城。心主包络，位居膻中，而代君行令，故为臣使之官。心志喜，心主代君宣布，故喜乐出焉。】
　　　　　玉机真脏论

　　因而喜大虚则肾气乘矣，怒则肝气乘矣，悲则肺气乘矣，恐则脾气乘矣，忧则心气乘矣，此其道也。故病有五，五五二十五变。及其传化，传乘之名也。　　 【注　因而喜大则心气虚而肾气乘于心矣，怒则肝气伤而肺气乘于肝，思则脾气伤而肝气乘于脾，恐则肾气伤而脾气乘于肾，忧则肺气伤而心气乘于肺矣。如一脏虚而受乘，即传之五脏，五脏有五变，则五五二十五变矣。如喜大而肾气乘心，心即传肺，肺传肝，肝传脾，脾传肾，是五脏传化，亦各乘其所胜。故曰，传者乘之名也。】[3p]

Secret Classic of Linglan

The center of the chest (Xuan Zhong) is the official representing the minister; joy and happiness are emitted from there.
[Note: The center of the chest is the palace of the heart. The heart encompasses and is situated in the center of the chest, serving the emperor by issuing commands, thus it is the official representing the minister. When the heart is joyful, it acts on behalf of the emperor, hence joy and happiness are emitted from there.]

True Essence of the Jade Mechanism

Therefore, if joy is excessive, the kidney energy is activated; if angry, the liver energy is activated; if sad, the lung energy is activated; if fearful, the spleen energy is activated; if worried, the heart energy is activated; this is its principle. Thus, there are five diseases, and five times five equals twenty-five transformations. When they transmit and transform, this is called the transmission of energy.
[Note: If joy is excessive, heart energy is depleted, and kidney energy acts on the heart; if angry, liver energy is harmed and lung energy acts on the liver; if pondering, spleen energy is harmed, and liver energy acts on the spleen; if fearful, kidney energy is harmed, and spleen energy acts on the kidney; if worried, lung energy is harmed, and heart energy acts on the lung. If one organ is depleted and receives transmission, it affects the five organs, which have five transformations, thus five times five equals twenty-five transformations. If joy is excessive and kidney energy acts on the heart, the heart transmits to the lung, lung transmits to the liver, liver transmits to the spleen, and spleen transmits to the kidney; this is the transmission and transformation of the five organs, with each overcoming its corresponding counterpart. Therefore, it is said that transmission is the name for the act of riding upon.][3p]

　　　　　举痛论

　　百病生于气也，怒则气上，喜则气缓，悲则气消，恐则气下，寒则气收，炅则气泄，惊则气乱，劳则气耗，思则气结。怒则气逆，甚则呕血及飧泄，故气上矣。喜则气和志达，荣卫通利，故气缓矣。悲则心系急，肺布叶举而上焦不通，荣卫不散，热气在中故气消矣。恐则精却，却则上焦闭，闭则气还，还则下焦胀，故气不行矣。寒则腠理闭，气不行，故气收矣。炅则腠理开，荣卫通，汗大泄，故气泄矣。惊则心无所倚神无所归，虑无所定，故气乱矣。劳则喘息汗出，外内皆越，故气耗矣。思则心有所存，神有所归，正气留而不行，故气结矣。[4p]

Discussion on Pain

All illnesses arise from emotions. When angry, qi rises; when joyful, qi softens; when sad, qi dissipates; when fearful, qi descends; when cold, qi contracts; when hot, qi leaks; when startled, qi becomes chaotic; when overworked, qi is diminished; when overly contemplative, qi becomes stagnant. Anger causes qi to reverse, and if severe, it can lead to vomiting blood and diarrhea, thus qi rises. Joy harmonizes qi and enhances spirit, leading to a relaxed state, hence qi softens. Sadness causes the heart to be anxious, the lungs to lift, and the upper jiao to be obstructed, preventing the dispersal of nutrients and resulting in stagnant heat within, hence qi dissipates. Fear causes essence to retreat, which can close off the upper jiao, causing qi to revert and the lower jiao to bloat, thus qi does not circulate. Cold closes the pores, leading to stagnation, hence qi contracts. Heat opens the pores, allowing for smooth circulation, resulting in significant sweating, thus qi leaks. Startle leads to a mind without support and a spirit without resting place, causing worries to be unsettled, hence qi becomes chaotic. Overexertion leads to panting and sweating, with both external and internal flow disrupted, thus qi is diminished. Contemplation causes the heart to latch onto thoughts and the spirit to have a resting point, retaining upright qi which does not circulate, hence qi becomes stagnant.[4p]

　　【注　怒为肝志，肝主藏血，怒则肝气上逆，故甚则呕血；木气乘脾，故为飧泄。脾位中州，肝脏居下，故呕血飧泄，皆为气上也。喜则志意和达，荣卫疏通，其气舒徐而和缓矣。心气并于肺则悲，心悲气并，则心系急，而上焦之气不通，荣卫不能行散矣。气郁于中则热，中气不运行，故潜消也。恐伤肾，是以精气退却而不能上升。膻中为气之海，上出于肺，以司呼吸，然其原出于下焦，故精气却则上焦闭，闭则生升之气还归于下而下焦胀矣。上下之气不相交通，故气不行矣。寒气客于腠理，则腠理闭而气不通，故气收于内矣。炅则腠理开，汗大泄，则阳气从而外泄矣。惊则心气散而无所倚，神志越而无所归，思虑惑而无所定，故气乱矣。劳则肾气伤而喘息于内，阳气张而汗出于外，外内皆越，故气耗散矣。思则心神内存，正气留中而不行，故气结矣。】[5p]

Note: Anger pertains to the liver, which stores blood; when angry, the liver qi rises, which can lead to vomiting blood. The wood element affects the spleen, resulting in diarrhea. The spleen is located in the central region, while the liver is situated below; thus, both vomiting blood and diarrhea are manifestations of upward qi. Joy brings harmony and openness to the mind, allowing the qi to flow smoothly and gently. When the heart qi merges with the lungs, it leads to sadness; if heart sadness intensifies, the heart becomes anxious, causing the upper body's qi to become obstructed and the defensive qi to fail in dispersing. When qi is stagnant internally, it generates heat, and if the middle qi does not circulate, it leads to hidden consumption. Fear damages the kidneys, causing the essence and qi to retreat and fail to ascend. The zhongdan (chest area) serves as the sea of qi, rising from the lungs to control respiration, yet originally derives from the lower region; thus, if essence and qi retreat, the upper region closes, leading to an upward qi being redirected downward, causing distention in the lower area. With no exchange of qi between upper and lower, qi becomes stagnant. When cold qi invades the pores, the pores close and qi does not flow, resulting in internal retention. When heat opens the pores, excessive sweating occurs, causing yang qi to leak outward. Surprise scatters the heart qi, making it feel unanchored; the spirit becomes unsettled with nowhere to return, and thoughts become chaotic, leading to disarray in qi. Overexertion damages kidney qi, causing internal panting, while yang qi expands and sweating occurs externally, leading to imbalance between internal and external forces and dispersing qi. Excessive thinking retains the heart spirit within, causing righteous qi to stagnate and preventing its movement, thus resulting in qi stagnation.[5p]

　　　　　调经论

　　神有余则笑不休，神不足则悲。
　　 【注　心在志为喜，在声为笑，故有余则笑不休，不足则金气反胜而为悲。】　　血有余则怒，不足则恐。
　　 【注　肝志怒，故血有余则肝气盛而主怒。肾志恐，故血不足则母气衰而并于脾，故恐。】　　血并于上，气并于下，心烦惋，善怒。　　 【注　血并上则脉气实而心烦惋，气并于下则不舒气而多怒也。】
　　　　　大奇论

　　脉至如华者，令人善恐，不欲坐卧行立，常听，是小肠气予不足也，季秋而死。　　 【注　脉至如华者，如华之轻微也。小肠为心之腑而属丙火，其脉当来盛，反如华者，气予不足也。腑气不足则脏气亦虚，神虚则恐惧自失，神志不宁，故坐卧不安也。小肠之脉入耳中，属听宫，常有所听者，如耳作蝉鸣，或如钟磬声，皆虚证也。遇金水生旺之时而死。】[6p]

On Regulating Menstruation

When the spirit is abundant, laughter is unending; when the spirit is deficient, sadness arises.
[Note: Joy is associated with the heart’s will, reflecting as laughter when abundant, while deficiency can lead to excessive metal energy resulting in sadness.] Blood in abundance leads to anger; insufficient blood results in fear.
[Note: Anger is associated with the liver’s will; therefore, when blood is abundant, liver energy is strong, causing anger. The will of the kidneys relates to fear; thus, when blood is insufficient, the maternal energy weakens and is shared with the spleen, resulting in fear.] Blood accumulating upward causes distress, while energy accumulating downward leads to increased anger.
[Note: Blood accumulating upward makes the pulse strong and the heart distressed; energy's accumulation downward prevents smooth flow, resulting in excessive anger.]

On Great Oddities

A pulse that feels like flower petals makes one prone to fear; one does not wish to sit, lie down, walk, or stand, and is always listening—this signifies a deficiency in the small intestine’s energy, leading to death in late autumn.
[Note: A pulse that feels like flower petals indicates delicacy. The small intestine, as a subsidiary of the heart, belongs to the fire element; its pulse should be robust, but if it feels like flower petals, it means energy is deficient. If the energy of the viscera is insufficient, the energy of the organs is also weak, leaving the spirit vulnerable and fearful, resulting in restlessness. The small intestine's pulse connects to the ear, which belongs to the sense of hearing; when one always hears sounds like cicadas or bells, it is a sign of deficiency. Death can occur at the time when metal and water flourish.][6p]

　　　　　脉解篇

　　阳明所谓甚则厥，恶人与火，闻木音则惕然而惊者，阳气与阴气相薄，水火相恶，故惕然而惊也。　　【注　阳明气厥，则阳明之脉病，乃恶人与火，闻木音则惕然而惊也。】　　少阳所谓少气善怒者，阳气不治，阳气不治则阳气不得出，肝气当治而未得，故善怒。善怒者，名曰煎厥。　　 【注　少阳主气，秋时阳气下降，而不治于外，则少阳之气亦不得出，故少气也。厥阴肝气与少阳标本相合，少阳之气不得出，则肝气当治而亦未得矣。肝气内郁，故善怒。煎厥者，焦烦颠倒也。】　　所谓恐如人将捕之者，秋气万物未有毕去，阴气少，阳气入，阴阳相薄故恐也。　　 【注　秋时阳气虽入，而阴气尚少，故万物虽衰而未尽去。阴气虽少，当正出之时，而与阳气之入相薄，则少阳厥阴之气皆伤，肝气虚则恐。胆病者心下淡淡，如人将捕之。】[7p]

Pulse Diagnosis

The Yangming (Greater Yang) speaks of severe conditions leading to Qi collapse. The malevolent, akin to fire, upon hearing the sound of wood, startles and trembles. This is because Yang energy and Yin energy are weakened against each other, causing an adverse relation between water and fire, hence the disturbance and fear.

Note: When Yangming Qi collapses, it indicates a disease of the Yangming pulse; evil people relate to fire, and the fear caused by the sound of wood signifies disturbance and alarm.

The Shaoyang (Lesser Yang) refers to insufficient Qi leading to a propensity for anger. When Yang energy is not rectified, it cannot be released. The liver Qi needs to be treated but has not been; thus, it leads to anger. This propensity for anger is referred to as "boiling Qi collapse."

Note: Shaoyang governs Qi. In autumn, as Yang energy decreases and is not expressed outwardly, Shaoyang energy cannot be released, leading to insufficient Qi. The liver Qi connects with the lesser and greater Yang; when Shaoyang energy is not released, liver Qi must be treated but remains unaddressed. The internal stagnation of liver Qi results in anger. "Boiling Qi collapse" represents deep frustration and reversal.

As for the concept of fear, it is akin to being hunted. In autumn, as the Qi diminishes but has not completely vanished, with insufficient Yin and incoming Yang, there is weakened interaction between Yin and Yang, leading to fear.

Note: Although Yang energy enters during autumn, Yin energy remains scant, so while all things decline, they have not entirely disappeared. Even with insufficient Yin, it is about to emerge, but when in conflict with the incoming Yang, both Shaoyang and Jueyin energies are harmed, leading to a deficiency in liver Qi and resulting in fear. In gallbladder ailments, the person feels a vague discomfort beneath the heart, as if being hunted.[7p]

　　　　　四时刺逆从论

　　夏刺肌肉，血气内却，令人善恐。
　　 【注　夏气在孙络，而使之溢于肌中，则血气虚却于内矣。阳明脉虚则恐，如人将捕之。】　　夏刺筋骨，血气上逆，令人善怒。
　　 【注　夏气浮长于上，而反逆之使下，则气郁不疏而使人善怒也。】[8p]

On the Seasonal Needle Techniques and Their Reversals

In summer, needling the muscles causes the blood and qi to retreat inward, making one prone to fear.
[Note: The summer energy affects the sinews, causing them to swell within the muscles, leading to a deficiency of blood and qi inside. When the Yangming pulse is weak, fear arises, as if one were about to be captured.]

In summer, needling the bones causes the blood and qi to rise inversely, making one prone to anger.
[Note: The summer energy is abundant and upward, and its reversal leads to stagnation of qi, making one easily angered.][8p]

　　　　　经脉别论

　　有所堕恐，喘出于肝，淫气害脾。有所惊恐，喘出于肺，淫气伤心。　　 【注　堕则伤筋，肝主筋，故喘出于肝。木胜土，故淫气害脾。惊则气乱，故喘出于肺。肺者心之盖，故淫气伤心。】　　疾走恐惧，汗出于肝。
　　 【注　疲劳伤筋，故汗出于肝。】
　　　　　宣明五气论

　　胃为气逆，为哕，为恐。胆为怒。
　　 【注　胃受肺之寒气所逆，而欲复出于胃，故为哕。胃之逆气，下并于肾则为恐。盖肾于胃戊癸相合也。胆为中正之官，性秉刚决，病则气郁而为怒。】　　五精所并：精气并于心则喜，并于肺则悲，并于肝则忧，并于脾则畏，并于肾则恐，是谓五并，虚而相并者也。　　 【注　心为阳脏，阴精并之故喜。肺虚而肝气并于肺则悲，肝虚而脾气并于肝则忧，脾虚而肾气并于脾则畏。阴气少，阳气入阴，阴阳相薄故恐也。】　　阳入之阴则静，阴出之阳则怒。[9p]

Discussion on Meridians

Fear can lead to a downward spiral, causing wheezing related to the liver, while excessive emotional energy damages the spleen. Shock leads to fear, causing wheezing related to the lungs, and excessive emotional energy harms the heart.

Note: Injury leads to damage in the tendons, with the liver governing the tendons, which is why wheezing is associated with the liver. Wood overcomes earth, and thus excessive emotional energy harms the spleen. Shock causes chaotic energy, leading to wheezing from the lungs. The lungs cover the heart, hence excessive emotional energy harms the heart.

When one experiences fear due to running rapidly, sweat emerges from the liver.

Note: Fatigue injures the tendons, thus sweat emerges from the liver.

Discussion on the Five Energies

The stomach experiences reversed qi, leading to belching and fear. The gallbladder is associated with anger.

Note: The stomach is affected by the cold qi of the lungs, causing a desire for it to be expelled, leading to belching. When the stomach's reversed qi descends to the kidneys, it results in fear. This is because the kidneys integrate with the stomach's energies. The gallbladder serves as the central authority, characterized by decisiveness; when ill, its qi becomes stagnated, resulting in anger.

The five essences combine: when essence and qi converge in the heart, it leads to joy; in the lungs, to sadness; in the liver, to worry; in the spleen, to fear; and in the kidneys, to terror, known as the five combinations, which are empty yet interrelated.

Note: The heart is a yang organ; its essence is yin, which causes joy. When the lungs are deficient and the liver energy combines with the lungs, it causes sadness; when the liver is weak and the spleen energy combines with the liver, it leads to worry; when the spleen is deficient and the kidney energy combines with the spleen, it results in fear. A deficiency of yin leads to the influx of yang into yin, causing a weakening of the balance and thus fear.

When yang enters yin, there is tranquility; when yin emerges, there is anger.[9p]

　　 【注　阳分之邪入阴，则病者静，盖阴盛则静也。阴分之邪出阳，则病者多怒，盖阳盛则怒也。】　　五邪所见：春得秋脉，夏得冬脉，长夏得春脉，秋得夏脉，冬得长夏脉，名曰阴出之阳，病善怒不治，是为五邪皆同，命死不治。　　 【注　春弦夏钩，秋毛冬石，五脏阴阳之正气也。反得所胜之脉者，邪贼盛而见于脉也。在内所伤之脏气，而外见于脉，故名之曰阴出之阳。邪出于脉则血有余，经曰血有余则怒，此正气为邪气所胜，故为不治。所谓不治者，谓五脉皆为邪胜也。如五脏之气为邪所胜，见四时相克之脉，皆为死不治矣。】[10p]

The text discusses the relationship between the "yin" and "yang" aspects of illness in traditional Chinese medicine. It explains that when the evil from the yang enters the yin, the patient becomes tranquil, as an excess of yin leads to stillness. Conversely, when the evil from the yin exits the yang, the patient becomes easily angered, as an excess of yang causes anger.

It describes the five types of evils: spring gaining autumn's pulse, summer gaining winter's pulse, late summer gaining spring's pulse, autumn gaining summer's pulse, and winter gaining late summer's pulse. This condition is referred to as "yang emerging from yin," leading to anger that is hard to treat, indicating an alignment of all five evils and resulting in fatality if untreated.

The text also notes that the characteristics of the seasons—spring representing strings, summer representing hooks, autumn representing fur, and winter representing stones—correspond to the proper qi of the five organs in yin and yang. When the pulse reflects the overcoming of the proper state, it indicates that the evil has become dominant. This imbalance leads to disturbances in the internal organ qi, reflecting on the pulse, thus being named "yang emerging from yin." When the evil exits through the pulse, it shows an excess of blood, aligning with the saying that "an excess of blood leads to anger." This imbalance is characterized by the proper qi being overwhelmed by the evil qi, marking it as a condition that is difficult to remedy. The idea of "untreatable" signifies that the pulses indicate a dominance of the evil. If the qi of the five organs is also overtaken by the evil, thus indicating opposing pulses according to the seasons, it indicates a situation that is fatal and untreatable.[10p]

　　　　　风论

　　心风之状，多汗恶风，焦绝，善怒吓，赤色，病甚则言不可快。诊在口，其色赤。　　 【注　心为火脏，风淫则火盛，故唇舌焦而津液绝。风化木，木火交炽，故善怒吓。心主舌，病甚则舌本强而言不可快。】　　肝风之状，多汗恶风，善悲，色微苍，嗌干善怒，时憎女子。诊在目下，其色青。　　 【注　肝开窍于目而主泣，故善悲。风木合邪，则火热盛而嗌干，肝气病，故善怒。】
　　　　　病能论

　　帝曰：有病怒狂者，此病安生？
　　 【注　肝虽顺传于心，而不得相生之正气，反受肝之寒邪，寒凌心火，故为怒狂。】　　岐伯曰：生于阳也。帝曰：阳何以使人狂？岐伯曰：阳气者，因暴折而难决，故善怒也，病名曰阳厥。　　 【注　肝气上逆则阳气暴折而不得出，阳气难于流行则肝气亦未得而治，故善怒也。】[11p]

Discussion on Wind

The condition of the heart wind often features excessive sweating and sensitivity to drafts, leading to a scorched feeling, quick to anger and fear, with a reddish color; when the illness is severe, the speech becomes hesitant. Diagnosis occurs in the mouth, where the color appears red. 【Note: The heart is a fire organ; when wind is excessive, the fire becomes rampant, resulting in scorched lips and a lack of bodily fluids. The wind congeals with wood, and the fire in wood becomes intense, which explains the quickness to anger and fright. The heart governs the tongue, so when ill, the tongue appears strong but speech becomes hesitant.】

The condition of the liver wind often features excessive sweating and sensitivity to drafts, a tendency to weep, and a slightly pale color; the throat is dry and quick to anger, with a periodic dislike for women. Diagnosis occurs under the eyes, where the color appears bluish. 【Note: The liver opens to the eyes and governs weeping, hence the tendency to weep. When wind and wood align as a disturbance, the fire becomes overly intense, which leads to throat dryness and anger due to liver qi illness.】

Discussion on Illness

The Emperor asked: For someone suffering from anger and madness, where does this illness arise? 【Note: Though the liver transmits smoothly to the heart, it does not receive the right energies to produce life-force, instead succumbing to the cold evils of the liver, which suppress the heart fire, resulting in anger and madness.】 Qi Bo replied: It arises from yang. The Emperor asked: How does yang cause madness? Qi Bo answered: Yang energy, when violently stifled and difficult to release, leads to a propensity for anger; this condition is termed 'yang collapse.' 【Note: When liver qi rises against the flow, the yang energy is violently stifled, making it hard to circulate, thus liver qi is also unable to be treated, which results in the propensity for anger.】[11p]

　　　　　脏气法时论

　　肝病者，两胁下痛引小腹，令人善怒，虚则目(目巟)(目巟)无所见，耳无所闻，善恐，如人将捕之。　　 【注　虚者，精气夺也。少阳经脉入耳中，故无所闻。肝病者，心下淡淡，如人将捕之。】
　　　　　痹论

　　淫气忧思，痹聚在心。
　　 【注　淫气忧思，则心气不藏，而痹聚在心矣。】
　　　　　诊要经终论

　　春刺秋分，筋挛，逆气环为咳嗽，病不愈，令人时惊，又且哭。　　 【注　病在肝而反伤其肺，是以筋挛。血气环逆，故咳嗽。魂魄不安，故哭也。】　　夏刺冬分，病不愈，令人少气，时欲怒。　　 【注　夏月阳气外张，而反逆藏于冬分，故不惟病不愈，而更令人少气善怒也。】[12p]

On the Method of Treating Internal Disorders

For those with liver ailments, pain beneath both ribs radiates to the lower abdomen, leading to irritability. If deficient, one may see nothing with the eyes and hear nothing with the ears, and be filled with fear, as if being hunted. [Note: Deficiency occurs when vital energy is drained. The Shaoyang channel enters the ears, hence the inability to hear. In liver disease, there is a feeling of lightness below the heart, as if being hunted.]

On Obstructions

Indulgent emotions and worries cause blockages in the heart. [Note: Indulgent emotions and worries prevent the heart's energy from consolidating, leading to blockages in the heart.]

On Essential Methods of Diagnosis

In spring, if acupuncture is applied, at the Autumn Equinox, muscle spasms and reverse qi cause coughing. If the illness does not improve, it leads to bouts of shock and crying. [Note: The disease resides in the liver, which in turn affects the lungs, causing muscle spasms. Blood and qi flow in reverse, causing coughing. Troubled spirits lead to crying.]

In summer, acupuncture during the Winter Solstice does not improve the illness, leading to diminished energy and episodes of anger. [Note: In summer, the yang energy emerges, but it reverses and hides during the Winter Solstice, thus not only does the illness remain, but it also diminishes energy and increases irritability.][12p]

　　　　　气交变大论

　　岁土太过，雨湿流行，肾水受邪，民病意不乐。　　 【注　肾藏志，志不舒，故意不乐。】　　岁木太过，甚则忽忽善怒。
　　 【注　善怒，肝志之病也。】
　　岁土不及，民病善怒。
　　 【注　风木之病。】

　　　　　五常政大论

　　发生之纪，其病怒。
　　 【注　怒，肝气盛也。】
　　伏明之纪，其病昏惑悲忘，从水化也。　　 【注　心神不足也。】
　　太阳司天，火气高明，喜悲。
　　 【注　火热铄金也。】

　　　　　至真要大论

　　太阳司天，民病善悲。
　　【注　阳热中盛之证。】
　　太阳之复，善悲，甚则入心，善忘善悲。　　 【注　木火之气衰也。】[13p]

Discussion on the Changes of Qi

In a year when earth is excessive, rain becomes abundant and causes dampness to flow, the kidney's water is affected by evils, leading to the people feeling unhappy. (Note: The kidney stores will; if will is not at ease, then unhappiness arises.)
In a year when wood is excessive, the result is suddenly heightened anger. (Note: Anger is a disease of the liver's will.)
In a year when earth is insufficient, the people develop a tendency towards anger. (Note: This is a disease caused by wind and wood.)

Discussion on the Great Principles of Governance

In the epoch of emergence, the sickness manifests as anger. (Note: Anger is due to excessive liver qi.)
In the era of hidden brightness, the sickness manifests as confusion, bewilderment, and sorrow, stemming from the transformation of water. (Note: This indicates insufficient heart spirit.)
When the sun governs the heavens, the fire's qi is elevated, resulting in joy and sorrow. (Note: The heat of fire refines metal.)

Discussion on the Essential Truths

When the sun governs the heavens, the people suffer from excessive sorrow. (Note: This is evidence of extreme yang heat within.)
In the resurgence of the sun, there is a tendency towards sorrow; if excessive, it penetrates the heart, leading to forgetfulness and heightened sorrow. (Note: This indicates a decline in the energies of wood and fire.)[13p]

　　　　　解精微论

　　悲哀则泣下，泣下水所由生。水宗者，积水也。积水者，至阴也。至阴者，肾之精也。宗精之水所以不出者，是精持之也。辅之裹之，故水不行也。　　 【注　悲哀则动其心志，故泣下，而水所由生。水宗者，宗脉之所聚，上液之道也。肾脏之精水，由宗脉而上通于心外，注于目，故曰目者宗脉之所聚也。如志不悲，则精持于下，辅之裹之，水精不出于宗脉，故水不行于上也。】　　夫水之精为志，火之精为神，水火相感，神志俱悲，是以目之水生也。故谚言曰，心悲名曰志悲，志与心精共凑于目也。　　 【注　心之所之谓之志，心志之合一也。心者五脏之专精，故水精与心精，共凑于目而为泣。】　　是以俱悲则神气传于心，精不上传于志而志独悲，故泣出也。　　 【注　精不上传于志而志独悲于上，故泣出也。】　　泣涕者，脑也。脑者，阴阴：《太素》卷二十九水论作「阳」。也。髓者，骨之充也。[14p]

On the Elucidation of Subtlety

Sadness leads to tears, with tears being the source of moisture. The essence of water is accumulation; it is the ultimate yin. The ultimate yin is the essence of the kidneys. The reason the essence of water does not flow is that it is retained. Wrapped and contained, thus the water does not circulate.

[Note: Sadness stirs the heart and will, causing tears to flow, which is the source of water. The essence of water refers to the gathering of the channels, the path of the upper fluid. The essence of the kidney-water, gathered through the channels, rises to connect with the heart externally and flows to the eyes, hence the eyes are where the channels converge. If the will is not sad, then the essence remains below, wrapped and contained, and the water essence does not emerge from the channels, thus it does not flow upward.]

The essence of water is the will, and the essence of fire is the spirit. When water and fire interact, both spirit and will are saddened, hence the moisture in the eyes is produced. Therefore, the saying goes: when the heart is sad, it is called a sad will, as the spirit and essence of the heart converge in the eyes.

[Note: The focus of the heart is referred to as the will; it is the unity of heart and will. The heart is the specialized essence of the five organs, thus the essence of water and that of the heart coalesce in the eyes to produce tears.]

Thus, when both are sad, the spirit energy transmits to the heart, but the essence does not ascend to the will, so the will is exclusively sad, resulting in tears being shed.

[Note: The essence does not ascend to the will, so the will is exclusively sad, hence tears are shed.]

Tears and weeping relate to the brain. The brain is associated with yin: "Tai Su" (Great Origin) Vol. 29, on water, states it as "yang." The marrow is the filling of the bones.[14p]

故脑渗为涕。志者，骨之主也，是以水流而涕从之者，其行类也。　　 【注　骨之精髓充于骨髓，从骨空而上通于脑，故脑渗之为涕也。夫志者骨之主也，是以水流而涕从之者，其行与志悲而肾精出于目之为泣者，相同类也。】　　夫涕之与泣者，譬如人之兄弟，急则俱死，生则俱生，其志以早悲，是以涕泣俱出而横行行：《素问》解精微论王冰注：「行恐当为流」。也。夫人涕泣俱出而相从者，所属之类也。　　 【注　涕泣俱出而相从者，缘肾脏所属之同类也。】　　夫泣不出者，哭不悲也。不泣者，神不慈也。神不慈则志不悲，阴阳相持，泣安能独来？夫志悲者，惋惋则冲阴，冲阴则志去目，志去则神不守精，精神去目，涕泣出也。　　 【注　阴阳相持，谓水火之神志，主持于内，则精不出也。冲阴，谓志上冲于脑也。夫目系上属于脑，故志上冲阴则志去走于目，志去则神不独守其精，精神并去，出于目而涕泣皆出也。】[15p]

The brain's seepage manifests as tears. The will (or longing) is the master of the bones; thus, as water flows, tears follow suit, echoing their nature.

The essence of the bones is contained in the marrow, which rises from the bone cavity to connect with the brain; hence, the brain's seepage results in tears. The will, as the master of the bones, allows for the flow of water, thus tears emerge alongside it. The actions of will and sorrow closely resemble one another, as the essence from the kidneys spills from the eyes to create weeping.

Tears and weeping are akin to brothers; in times of urgency, they both perish, and in times of life, they both thrive together. If one's will is filled with early sorrow, both tears and weeping emerge and flow together.

When tears and weeping emerge together, it is due to their belonging to the same category associated with the kidneys.

If there are no tears, it signifies that the cry lacks sorrow. When one does not weep, the spirit lacks compassion. Without compassion, the will cannot express sorrow; when Yin and Yang hold each other in balance, how can tears come alone? When the will is sorrowful, the overwhelming emotion pushes against the Yin, which disturbs the will and thus drains the spirit. If the spirit does not guard the essence, it departs from the eyes, leading to the release of tears and weeping.

The balance of Yin and Yang refers to the harmonious interplay of the spirit and will internalized, preventing the essence from leaking out. The overwhelming emotion refers to the will rising to the brain. The eyes are connected to the brain, thus when the will rises and pushes against the Yin, it causes the will to flee toward the eyes; if the will is lost, the spirit cannot guard its essence, leading to a release from the eyes, resulting in weeping.[15p]

　　　　　六元正纪大论

　　少阴所至为语笑。
　　 【注　此冬病之常也。】

　　　　　疏五过论

　　暴怒伤阴，暴喜伤阳。
　　 【注　暴怒则血并于阴，故伤阴。暴喜则气并于阳，故伤阳矣。】
　　　　灵枢经

　　　　　邪气脏腑病形篇[16p]

Six Principles and the Great Discussion

When the lesser yin arrives, it brings laughter and speech.
[Note: This is a common occurrence in winter illnesses.]

Commentary on Five Excesses

Violent anger injures yin, while extreme joy injures yang.
[Note: Violent anger causes blood to consolidate in yin, hence it injures yin. Extreme joy causes qi to consolidate in yang, hence it injures yang.]

Spiritual Pivot Scripture

Pathogenic Qi and the Symptoms of Organ Diseases[16p]

　　心脉缓甚为狂笑。
　　 【注　缓甚则心气有余，心藏神，神有余则笑不休。】
　　　　　本神篇

　　是故怵惕思虑则伤神，神伤则恐惧流淫而不止，因悲哀动中者，竭绝而失生。喜乐者，神惮散而不藏。愁忧者，气闭塞而不行。盛怒者，迷惑而不治。恐惧者，神荡惮而不收。　　 【注　思虑志意，皆心之所生，是以伤心脏之神气。】　　心怵惕思虑则伤神，神伤则恐惧自失，破(月囷)脱肉，毛悴色夭，死于冬。　　 【注　思虑，脾之情。如怵惕思虑则伤心脏之神，神伤则不能主持而恐惧自失。】　　脾忧愁而不解则伤意，意伤则悗乱，四肢不举，毛悴色夭，死于春。　　 【注　忧愁，肺之情。如忧愁不解则伤脾脏之意，意伤则悗乱而四肢不举。】　　肝悲哀动中则伤魂，魂伤则狂忘不精，不精则不正，当人阴缩而挛筋，两胁骨不举，毛悴色夭，死于秋。　　 【注　悲哀，肺之情。如悲哀动中则伤肝脏所藏之魂，魂伤则狂忘不精。[17p]

The heart's pulse, when it is excessively relaxed, leads to wild laughter.

Thus, anxiety and overthinking injure the spirit; when the spirit is hurt, fear and indulgence become uncontrollable, and deep sorrow leads to exhaustion and loss of life. Joy and happiness cause the spirit to scatter and not settle. Worry and sorrow lead to stagnation and impede the flow of energy. Intense anger results in confusion and inability to manage emotions. Fear causes the spirit to drift and become unsettled.

Anxiety and overthinking harm the heart's spirit. When the spirit is injured, fear leads to self-loss; it disrupts bodily coherence, causing the hair to dull and complexion to pale, resulting in death in winter.

Sorrow unresolved harms the spleen; when the heart is hurt, emotions become chaotic, and the limbs become weak, leading to death in spring.

Grief, when unresolved, injures the lungs; this affects the spleen's emotions, causing confusion and weakness in the limbs.

Deep sorrow within the liver harms the soul; when the soul is injured, it leads to madness and distraction, which disrupts physical alignment, causing the body to weaken and complexion to pale, resulting in death in autumn.[17p]

】　　肺喜乐无极则伤魄，魄伤则狂，狂者意不存人，皮革焦，毛悴色夭，死于夏。　　 【注　喜乐，心之情。如喜乐无极则伤肺脏之魄，魄伤则狂，狂则神亦惮散而意不存。】　　肾盛怒而不止则伤志，志伤则喜忘其前言，腰脊不可以俯仰屈伸，毛悴色夭，死于季夏。　　 【注　怒者，肝之情。如盛怒不止则伤肾脏之志，志伤则喜忘其前言。喜忘者，神志皆伤也。】　　恐惧而不解则伤精，精伤则骨酸痿厥，精时自下。是五脏主藏精者也，不可伤，伤则失守而阴虚，阴虚则无气，无气则死矣。　　 【注　恐伤肾，故恐惧不解则伤肾脏之精。肾主骨，故骨酸痿厥。精时自下者，脏气伤而不能藏也。】　　肝藏血，血舍魂。肝气虚则恐，实则怒。　　 【注　肝者将军之官，故气虚则恐，气实则怒。】　　心藏脉，脉舍神。心气虚则悲，实则笑不休。　　 【注　心气虚则悲盛，实则笑不休。】[18p]

The lungs thrive on joy and happiness, but excessive joy can harm the spirit; when the spirit is hurt, madness ensues. A mad person loses their sense of self, their skin becomes dull, their hair falls out, and they may die in summer.

The kidneys, when filled with unending anger, harm the will; when the will is harmed, joy causes one to forget previous intentions. The back cannot bend or stretch, the hair becomes brittle and the complexion pale, leading to death in late summer.

Fear and unresolved dread harm the essence; when the essence is harmed, the bones ache and weaken, and the essence descends. The five organs are the keepers of essence; if harmed, they lose their protective power, leading to yin deficiency, which results in a lack of energy, and ultimately death.

The liver stores blood, which shelters the soul. A deficiency in liver qi causes fear, while an excess results in anger.

The heart harbors the pulse, which hosts the spirit. When heart qi is deficient, it leads to deep sorrow; when it is abundant, it results in uncontrollable laughter.[18p]

　　　　　经脉篇

　　心主手厥阴心包络之脉，是动甚则胸胁支满，心中淡淡大动，面赤目黄，喜笑不休。　　 【注　胸胁支满，心中淡淡大动，面赤目黄，喜笑不休者，有余于内也。】　　肾足少阴之脉，气不足则善恐，心惕惕如人将捕之。　　 【注　此少阴肾脏之生气，厥逆于下而为病也。】[19p]

Meridian Text

The heart governs the hand's jueyin heart protector channel. When it is overly active, the chest and sides feel full, there is a faint but significant agitation in the heart, the face turns red and the eyes yellow, and one laughs incessantly. 【Note: The fullness in the chest and sides, the faint but significant agitation in the heart, the red face and yellow eyes, and the incessant laughter indicate excess within.】 The kidney's foot shaoyin channel, when its energy is deficient, leads to a propensity for fear, and the heart feels uneasy as if being hunted. 【Note: This indicates that the vital energy of the shaoyin kidney is disturbed downward and causes illness.】[19p]

　　　　　邪淫发梦篇

　　肝气盛则梦怒。
　　 【注　此邪干五形脏而形之于梦也。】
　　　　　行针篇

　　多阳者多喜，多阴者多怒。
　　 【注　心为阳中之太阳，肝为阴中之少阳，心主喜，肝主怒也。】
　　　　　百病始生篇

　　喜怒不节则伤脏，脏伤则病起于阴也。　　 【注　此形气外内之相应也。】

　　　　　邪客篇

　　天有风雨，人有喜怒。

　　　　　厥论

　　风痹淫泺，病不可已者，足如履冰，时如入汤中，股胫淫泺，烦心头痛，时呕时闷，眩已汗出，久则目眩，悲以喜恐，短气不乐，不出三年死也。　　 【注　风邪淫泺于上下，故病不可已。盖寒之则伤心主之火，热之则伤肾脏之阴，病不可治，故不可已也。悲以喜恐者，心肾之神志伤而悲泣也。短气者，伤其肾气也。不乐者，伤其心气也。】[20p]

Dream of Deviant Lust

When liver qi is excessive, one dreams of anger.
Note: This highlights the disturbances of the five organs manifested in dreams.

Acupuncture Treatise

Those with abundant yang have much joy; those with abundant yin have much anger.
Note: The heart is the greatest among yang, while the liver is lesser yang among yin; the heart governs joy, and the liver governs anger.

On the Beginning of All Illnesses

If joy and anger are unregulated, they damage the organs; when organs are damaged, illness arises from yin.
Note: This indicates the correspondence between the external and internal states of energy.

On Deviant Disturbances

In the heavens, there are winds and rains; in humans, there are joys and angers.

Discussion on Syncope

Wind dampness and indulgence in pleasure lead to ailments that cannot cease; the feet feel like walking on ice, while at times they feel like entering hot water. The thighs and legs are affected, causing headaches and restlessness, dizziness, sweating, and long-term symptoms like dim vision. The person experiences sorrow, joy, and fear, suffers shortness of breath and unhappiness; death follows within three years.
Note: The penetration of wind dampness affects both upper and lower regions, hence the persistence of illness. Cold damages the heart's fire, while heat damages the yin of the kidneys, making recovery difficult, thus the conditions cannot cease. The conjunction of sorrow, joy, and fear indicates harm to the spirit of the heart and kidneys, leading to weeping. Shortness of breath injures kidney energy, while unhappiness harms heart energy.[20p]

　　　　　本脏篇

　　五脏皆小者，少病，苦焦心，大愁忧。五脏皆大者缓于事，难使以忧。　　 【注　五脏所以藏精神血气魂魄志意者也，故小则血气收藏而少病。小则神志畏怯，故苦焦心，大忧愁也。大则神志充足，故缓于事，难使以忧。】
　　　　　五癃津液别篇

　　五脏六腑之津液，尽上渗于目，心悲气并则心系急，心系急则肺举，肺举则液上溢。夫心系与肺不能尽举，乍上乍下，故咳而泣出矣。　　 【注　心悲则脏腑之气，皆上并于心，听令于君主也。气并于心则心系急，心系急则肺举，肺乃心之盖也。肺举则液上溢，肺主气而水随气行也。心系与肺不能尽举，乍上乍下，下则为咳，上则泣出矣。】[21p]

On the Organs

When all five organs are small, there are few illnesses; the heart suffers from heat and anxiety, leading to great sorrow. When all five organs are large, they handle affairs more slowly, making it difficult to induce worry. (Note: The five organs serve to store spirit, blood, qi, soul, and will. When they are small, the blood and qi are contained, resulting in fewer illnesses. Small organs cause the spirit to become timid, leading to the heart suffering and great sorrow. When the organs are large, the spirit is ample, so they handle affairs slowly and are difficult to worry.)

On the Fluids of the Five Organs and Six Bowels

The fluids of the five organs and six bowels seep upward to the eyes; when the heart is sad and the qi is combined, the heart becomes anxious. When the heart is anxious, the lungs rise; when the lungs rise, the fluids overflow. The heart and lungs cannot fully rise together, alternating up and down, hence cough and tears come forth. (Note: When the heart is sad, the qi of the organs all rises to the heart, obeying the commands of the sovereign. When qi rises to the heart, it becomes anxious; when anxious, the lungs rise, which serve as the covering for the heart. When the lungs rise, the fluids overflow, as the lungs govern qi and water follows the rising qi. The heart and lungs cannot fully rise together, hence the alternation leads to coughing and tearful outpouring.)[21p]

　　　　扁鹊难经

　　　　　五积具五志

　　假令得肝脉，其外证善洁，面青，善怒；其内证脐左有动气，按之牢若痛；其病四肢满闭，淋溲便难，转筋。有是者肝也，无是者非也。　　假令得心脉，其外证面赤，口干，喜笑；其内证脐上有动气，按之牢若痛；其病烦心心痛，掌中热而啘。有是者心也，无是者非也。　　假令得脾脉，其外证面黄，善噫，善思，善味；其内证当脐有动气，按之牢若痛；其病腹胀满，食不消，体重节痛，怠堕嗜卧，四肢不收。有是者脾也，无是者非也。　　假令得肺脉，其外证面白善嚏，悲愁不乐，欲哭；其内证脐右有动气，按之牢若痛；其病喘咳，洒淅寒热。有是者肺也，无是者非也。　　假令得肾脉，其外证面黑，善恐欠；其内证脐下有动气，按之牢若痛。其病逆气小腹急痛，泄如下重，足胫寒而逆。有是者肾也，无是者非也。[22p]

Bian Que's Difficult Classic

On the Five Accumulations and Their Corresponding Emotions

If one finds the liver pulse, the external signs are happy and clean, the face is bluish, and there is a tendency to anger; the internal sign is that there is moving energy to the left of the navel, which feels firm and painful upon pressure; the symptoms of the disease include fullness and closure of the limbs, difficulty in urination and defecation, and cramps. If these exist, it indicates a liver condition; if not, then it does not.

If one finds the heart pulse, the external signs are a red face, dry mouth, and a tendency to laughter; the internal sign shows moving energy above the navel, which feels firm and painful upon pressure; the symptoms of the disease include anxiety, heart pain, warmth in the palms, and restlessness. If these exist, it indicates a heart condition; if not, then it does not.

If one finds the spleen pulse, the external signs are a yellow face, tendency to burp, deep thinking, and a fondness for flavors; the internal sign shows moving energy at the navel, which feels firm and painful upon pressure; the symptoms of the disease include abdominal fullness, inability to digest food, a heavy body with joint pain, lethargy, and a desire to lie down. If these exist, it indicates a spleen condition; if not, then it does not.

If one finds the lung pulse, the external signs are a pale face, tendency to sneeze, sadness, and unhappiness, with a desire to cry; the internal sign shows moving energy to the right of the navel, which feels firm and painful upon pressure; the symptoms of the disease include coughing, wheezing, and alternating chills and fever. If these exist, it indicates a lung condition; if not, then it does not.

If one finds the kidney pulse, the external signs are a dark face and a tendency towards fear; the internal sign shows moving energy below the navel, which feels firm and painful upon pressure; the symptoms of the disease include counterflow energy, urgent pain in the lower abdomen, diarrhea, coldness in the legs and shins, and counterflow. If these exist, it indicates a kidney condition; if not, then it does not.[22p]

　　　　伤寒论 【汉　张机】

　　　　　恐怖之脉

　　问曰：人病恐怖者，其脉何状？
　　师曰：脉行如循丝累累然，其面白脱色也。
　　　　中藏经 【汉　华佗】

　　　　　情欲成气痹

　　气痹者，愁思喜怒，过则气结于上，久而不消则伤肺，伤肺则生气渐衰而邪气愈胜，留于上则胸腹痹而不能食，注于下则腰脚重而不能行，攻于左则左不遂，冲于右则右不仁，贯于舌则不能言，遗于肠则不能溺，壅而不散则痛，流而不聚则麻。真经既损，难以医治。邪气不胜，易为痊愈。其脉右手寸口沉而迟濇者是也。宜节忧思以养气，慎怒以全真，最为良矣。[23p]

Treatise on Febrile Diseases by Zhang Ji (Han Dynasty)

Pulse of Terror

Question: What does the pulse of a person suffering from terror look like?
Answer: The pulse moves like a tangled thread, and the face is pale and discolored.

Classic of Internal Medicine by Hua Tuo (Han Dynasty)

Emotional Desires Lead to Qi Stagnation

Qi stagnation arises from excessive sorrow, joy, anger, and thoughts, resulting in the qi becoming blocked above. If it persists, it harms the lungs; when the lungs are damaged, the vital qi gradually diminishes, allowing the pathogenic qi to dominate. If it remains above, it causes fullness in the chest and abdomen, leading to an inability to eat; if it descends, it results in heaviness in the waist and feet, making movement difficult. If it attacks the left, the left side won't comply; if it strikes the right, there is numbness on the right; if it pierces the tongue, one cannot speak; if it affects the intestines, one cannot urinate. If it becomes congested and doesn't disperse, it causes pain; if it flows but does not gather, it causes numbness. When the genuine qi is depleted, treatment becomes difficult. If the pathogenic qi is not overpowering, recovery is easier. The pulse manifests as a deep, slow, and slippery right wrist. It is advisable to moderate worries to nurture qi, exercise caution in anger to preserve the genuine, which is the best approach.[23p]

　　　　　恐怖死证

　　肝绝汗出如水，恐惧不安，伏卧，目直面青者，八日死，又曰即时死。　　筋绝魂惊虚恐，手足爪甲青，呼骂不休者，八九日死。
　　　　脉诀 【晋　王叔和】

　　　　　脉法

　　肝脏歌曰：逆时生恚怒，顺候脉弦长。泣下为之液，声呼是本乡。　　三部俱弦肝有余，目中疼痛苦痃虚。怒气满胸常欲叫，翳蒙瞳子泪如珠。
　　　　千金方 【唐　孙思邈】

　　　　　邪热伤肾

　　羽音人呻而好恚，恚而喜忘，恍惚有所思，此为土克水，阳击阴，阴气伏而阳气起，起则热，热则实，实则怒，怒则忘，耳听无闻，四肢满急，小便赤黄，语音口动而不出，笑而看人，此为邪热伤肾，甚则不可治。若面黑黄耳不应，亦可治。[24p]

Fear of Death Diagnosis

When the liver is exhausted, sweat flows like water, accompanied by terror and unease; lying down with an ashen face and staring eyes, death occurs within eight days, sometimes referred to as immediate death. If the tendons are severed and the spirit is shocked with emptiness and fear, if the hands and feet are mottled blue, and one continues to shout and curse, death occurs within eight or nine days.
Pulsation Text (Jin Dynasty, Wang Shuhe)

Pulsation Method

The song of the liver states: Against time, it generates anger, while following the pulse, it is long and taut. Tears flow as its liquid; the call is from its homeland. When all three positions feel taut, there is excess in the liver, and there is pain and discomfort in the eyes. Anger fills the chest, always wanting to shout; the vision is dim, and tears flow like pearls.
Thousand Golden Prescriptions (Tang Dynasty, Sun Simiao)

Evil Heat Injuring the Kidneys

A person with a gentle voice may be prone to anger, forgetting joy; in a daze, they may have thoughts. This indicates earth overpowering water, yang striking yin, with yin energy submissive and yang energy rising. When it rises, it causes heat; heat creates fullness, fullness provokes anger, and anger leads to forgetfulness. Hearing becomes unresponsive, the limbs are anxious, urine is red and yellow, the speech moves but does not come forth, one laughs but looks at others; this indicates evil heat injuring the kidneys, and in severe cases, it may be untreatable. If the face appears black and yellow, and the ears do not respond, it can still be treated.[24p]

　　　　河间六书 【金　刘完素】

　　　　　笑病之原

　　笑，蕃茂鲜淑，舒荣彰显，火之化也，故喜为心火之志。喜极而笑者，犹燔烁火。喜而鸣，笑之象也。故病笑者火之甚。或心本不喜，因侮戏而笑者，俗谓之冷笑。由是违己心则喜笑涉人，非道而伐之，便惭然失志。或以轻手扰人颈腋腹胁股腘足趺，令人痒而笑者，由动乱扰挠火之用，静顺清谧水之化，皮肤彰显之分属火，嫩薄隐藏之分属水，以火用扰其水分，使人渐然失志而痒，则水衰火旺而为笑。以手自扰而不笑者，不羞不痒故也。然羞惭而痒者，心火之化。人失信志则羞惭者，水衰火实故也。志与信者，肾水之化。但痒而不羞，羞而不痒，皆不能为笑者，化微不能变动故也。[25p]

On the Origin of Laughter

Laughter is abundant, fresh, and virtuous, flourishing and becoming apparent; it is a transformation of fire, thus it is a manifestation of the heart's fiery intent. When joy reaches its peak, laughter emerges, akin to a burning flame. The sound of joy is also the symbol of laughter. Therefore, those who laugh due to illness harbor excessive fire. Some may not truly feel joy in their hearts but laugh due to mockery or jest; this is commonly referred to as a cold laugh. When one laughs against their own heart's sincerity, transgressing moral boundaries, it leads to a sense of shame and loss of resolve.

Moreover, when one lightly touches another's neck, armpits, abdomen, sides, thighs, calves, or feet, causing them to itch and laugh, this is a disturbance of fiery energy. The transformation of calm, tranquil waters is disrupted, and the skin, which represents fire, visibly reacts. The delicate and hidden aspects pertain to water; if fire disrupts the water's essence, the person gradually loses their resolve and feels itching, leading them to laugh, as water weakens and fire surges.

If one disturbs themselves but does not laugh, it is due to the absence of shame or itching. Yet, when one feels both ashamed and itchy, it signifies a transformation of the heart's fire. When a person loses their confidence and feels ashamed, it is because water diminishes and fire intensifies. The relationship between will and confidence relates to the transformation of kidney water. However, those who are itchy but not ashamed, or ashamed but not itchy, cannot laugh, as their subtle transformation is incapable of movement.[25p]

　　　　　悲病之原

　　悲，金肺之志，金木能令燥者火也。心火主于热，喜痛，故悲痛苦恼者，心神烦热躁乱而非清净，所以悲哭。而五液俱出者，火热亢极，而反兼水化制之故也。夫五脏者肝心脾肺肾，五脏之志者怒喜悲【一作忧】 　思恐。若志过度则劳伤本脏。凡五志所伤皆热。六欲者，眼耳鼻舌身意；七情者，喜怒哀乐爱恶欲 【一作好爱恶。】 肝之所伤，则皆属火热。所谓阳动阴静，故形神劳则躁不宁，静则清平。是故上善若水，下愚如火。先圣曰：六欲七情，为道之患，属火故也。如中风偏枯者，由心火暴甚，而水衰不能制之，则火能克金，金不能克木则肝木自甚，而兼于火热，则卒暴僵仆，多因五志七情过度而卒病也。又如酒醉而热，则五志七情竞起，故经曰：战栗惊惑、悲笑谵妄、歌唱骂詈、癫狂皆为热。故热甚癫狂者，皆此证也。[26p]

The Origin of Sorrow and Illness

Sorrow arises from the spirit of the metal element, and metal and wood can cause dryness, transforming into fire. The fire of the heart pertains to heat and joy in pain, hence when one experiences sorrow and anguish, the heart and spirit become disturbed and agitated, rather than clear and tranquil, leading to weeping. When the five bodily fluids are all released, it is due to an extreme excess of fiery heat, which is also countered by the transformation and regulation of water. The five organs are the liver, heart, spleen, lungs, and kidneys, and their corresponding emotions are anger, joy, sorrow (or worry), thought, and fear. When any emotion is excessive, it can injure the corresponding organ. All injuries from the five emotions result in heat. The six desires are the eyes, ears, nose, tongue, body, and mind; the seven emotions are joy, anger, sorrow, happiness, love, aversion, and desire. When the liver is affected, it relates to fiery heat. The saying goes: the yang is active while yin is still, hence when the form and spirit are overworked, they become restless and agitated; when at peace, they are clear and harmonious. Thus, the highest goodness is like water, while the greatest folly is like fire. The ancient sages said: the six desires and seven emotions are a concern for the Way, and they pertain to fire. Just as a stroke can lead to unevenness and withering, when the heart fire becomes excessively violent and water cannot rein it in, the fire can control metal, and metal cannot control wood, causing the liver wood to become excessive and combined with fiery heat, which can lead to sudden collapse and paralysis, often due to the overindulgence in the five emotions and seven feelings. Similarly, intoxication leads to heat, causing the five emotions and seven feelings to stir up, hence the classics say: tremors, confusion, sorrowful laughter, delirium, singing, and cursing madness are all caused by heat. Therefore, those with extreme heat and madness all bear this symptom.[26p]

　　　　儒门事亲 【元　张从政】

　　　　　九气感疾更相为治衍

　　天以气而焘，地以气而持。万物盈乎天地之间，咸以气而生。及其病也，莫不以气而得。且风之气，和平而璺启；热之气，暄而舒荣；火之气，炎暑而出行；湿之气，埃溽而负盈；燥之气，清劲而凄怆；寒之气，寒气而归藏。此六气时化司化之常也。及其变，风之气飘怒而反大凉，热之气大暄而反寒，火之气飘风燔燎而反霜凝，湿之气雷霆骤注而反烈风，燥之气散落而反湿，寒之气寒雪霜雹而反白埃，此六气之变也。故天久寒则治之以暑，天久凉则治之以暄，天久晦则治之以明，天久晴则治之以雨。夫天地之气，常则安，变则病。而况人禀天地之气，五运迭侵于其外，七情交战于其中，是以圣人啬气如持至宝，庸人役物而反伤太和。[27p]

Rituals of Filial Piety
(Yuan Dynasty - Zhang Congzheng)

The nine atmospheres influence illness and treat each other in succession.

Heaven is illuminated by its essence, and the earth is sustained by its atmosphere. All things flourish between heaven and earth, all born of this essence. When illness arises, it is also derived from this atmosphere. The essence of wind is gentle, opening yet subtle; the essence of heat is warm and comforting; the essence of fire brings extreme heat and encourages action; the essence of moisture is heavy and suffocating; the essence of dryness is clear and harsh; the essence of cold brings winter chill and leads to concealment. These six essences are the regular transformations of nature. When they change, the wind essence may become turbulent and restore great coolness; the heat essence may become overly warm and reverse to cold; the fire essence may bring fierce gales and return frost; the moisture essence may bring sudden thunderstorms and result in violent winds; the dry essence may disperse and create wetness; the cold essence may bring snow, frost, and hail and result in white dust. This is the transformation of the six essences. Therefore, if heaven is persistently cold, one regulates it with warmth; if heaven is persistently cool, one regulates it with heat; if heaven is persistently dark, one regulates it with light; if heaven is persistently clear, one regulates it with rain. The essences of heaven and earth remain stable in normalcy but become illnesses in change. Furthermore, humans receive the essences of heaven and earth, with the five movements repeatedly invading from outside and the seven emotions battling within; thus, the wise cherish the essence as one would a precious treasure, while the foolish exploit material things and inadvertently harm harmony.[27p]

此轩岐所以论诸痛皆因于气，百病皆生于气，遂有九气不同之说。气本一也，因所触而为九。所谓九者，怒喜悲恐寒暑惊思劳也。其言曰：怒则气逆，甚则呕血及飧泄，故气逆上矣。王太仆曰：怒则阳气逆上而肝木乘脾，故甚则呕血及飧泄也。喜则气和志达，荣卫通利，故气缓矣。悲则心系急，肺布叶举，而上焦不通，荣卫不散，热气在中，故气消矣。恐则精却，却则上焦闭，闭则气还，还则下焦胀，故气不行矣。王太仆云：恐则伤精却上而不下流，下焦阴气，亦迥环而不散，故聚而胀也。然上焦固禁，下焦气还，故气不行也。　《新校正》云：不行当作下行。寒则腠理闭，气下行，故气收矣。王太仆云：身凉则卫气沉，故皮肤之理，及渗泄之处，皆闭密而气不流行，卫气收敛于中而不散也。炅则腠理开，荣卫通，汗大出，故气泄矣。[28p]

This text discusses how all pains and diseases arise from "qi" (vital energy), leading to the theory of nine different types of qi. While qi is fundamentally one, it becomes nine due to various influences. The nine types refer to anger, joy, grief, fear, cold, heat, shock, contemplation, and labor.

It states: when angry, qi reverses; if severe, it can lead to vomiting blood and diarrhea, hence qi rises. Wang Taifu said that anger causes yang qi to rise and liver wood to overtake the spleen, explaining the severe symptoms. Joy harmonizes qi and enables the spirit, allowing for smooth circulation of protective qi, thus making qi gentle. Grief causes the heart to become urgent, leading to lung dysfunction and blockage in the upper section, where heat accumulates, causing qi to decrease. Fear results in the retention of essence, closing the upper section and leading to stagnation and swelling in the lower section, preventing qi from flowing. Wang Taifu noted that fear can harm essence, making it unable to descend, and the lower section's yin qi can also become stagnant, causing swelling. The upper section remains blocked, and the lower section’s qi returns, thus qi does not flow.

The text states: "not flowing" should be interpreted as "descending." Cold causes the pores to close, leading qi to descend and thus accumulate. Wang Taifu explained that if the body feels cold, the protective qi condenses, resulting in the pores and drainage points tightly closing, preventing qi from circulating, and protective qi gathering internally without dispersing. When it is hot, the pores open, allowing the protective and nourishing qi to circulate freely, leading to substantial sweating and hence the release of qi.[28p]

王太仆云：人在阳则舒，在阴则惨，故热则肤腠开发，荣卫大通，津液而汗大出也。惊则心无所依，神无所归，虑无所定，故气乱矣。劳则喘息汗出，内外皆越，故气耗矣。王太仆云：疲劳役则气奔速，故喘息；气奔速则阳外发，故汗出；内外皆逾越于常纪，故气耗损也。思则心有所存，神有所归，正气留而不行，故气结矣。王太仆云：系心不散，故气亦停留。此《素问》之论九气，其变甚详，其理甚明。然论九气所感之疾则略，惟论呕血及飧泄，余皆不言。惟《灵枢》论思虑悲哀喜乐愁忧盛怒恐惧而言其病。其言曰：智者之养生也，必顺四时而适寒暑，和喜怒而安居处，节阴阳而和刚柔，如是则邪辟不至而长生久视。是故怵惕思虑则伤神，神伤则恐惧，流淫而不止。因悲哀动中者，竭绝而失生。[29p]

Wang Taifu said: When people are in the sun, they feel comfort; when in the shade, they feel sadness. Therefore, when it is hot, the skin pores open, the nutrients and defenses flow freely, and fluids and sweat are expelled in large quantities. When startled, the heart has no support, the spirit has no place to return, and thoughts are unsettled; thus, the vital energy becomes chaotic. When overworked, there is shortness of breath and sweating, with both internal and external states becoming excessive; thus, the vital energy is depleted. Wang Taifu said: When fatigued and laboring, the vital energy runs swiftly, causing breathlessness; when the vital energy rushes, it manifests externally, leading to sweating; both internal and external exceed their normal limits, thus depleting the energy. When thinking, the heart has something to hold onto, the spirit has a place to return, and正气 (upright energy) remains and does not disperse, hence the energy becomes stagnant. Wang Taifu said: When the heart is focused and not scattered, the energy also remains stationary. This discussion in the "Suwen" on the nine types of qi is very detailed, and its principles are very clear. However, the discussion of diseases caused by the nine types of qi is brief; it only mentions vomiting blood and diarrhea, leaving out the rest. Only the "Ling Shu" discusses illnesses caused by excessive thoughts, sadness, joy, and other emotions, stating: A wise person who nurtures life must follow the four seasons, adapt to cold and heat, harmonize joy and anger, and settle in appropriate places, balancing yin and yang and harmonizing rigidity and softness; thus, evils do not approach, and longevity is achieved. Therefore, excessive anxiety and worry harm the spirit; when the spirit is harmed, fear arises and this results in unchecked desires. Because of sorrow, the energetic center becomes depleted, leading to loss of life.[29p]

喜乐者，神荡散而不藏。愁虑者，气闭塞而不行。盛怒者，神迷惑而不治。恐惧者，神荡惮而不收。怵惕思虑则伤神，神伤则恐惧自失，破(月囷)脱肉，毛瘁色夭，死于冬。脾忧愁而不解则伤意，意伤则悗乱，四肢不举，毛瘁色夭，死于春。肝悲哀动中则伤魂，魂伤则狂忘不精，不精则不正，当人阴缩而挛筋，两胁不举，毛瘁色夭，死于秋。肺喜乐无极则伤魄，魄伤则狂，狂者意不存人，皮革焦，毛瘁色夭，死于夏。肾盛怒而不止则伤志，志伤则喜忘其前言，腰脊不可俯仰屈伸，毛瘁色夭，死于季夏。恐惧而不解则伤精，精伤则骨酸痿厥，精时自下。是故五脏主藏精者也，不可伤，伤则失守而阴虚，虚则无气，无气则死矣。《灵枢》论神意魂魄志精所主之病，然无寒暑惊劳四证，余以是推而广之。[30p]

Joyful individuals disperse their spirit and do not conceal it. Those burdened with worry have their energy blocked and do not flow. Those filled with intense anger confuse their spirit and do not heal. Those in fear have their spirit shaken and do not gather. Overthinking and anxiety harm the spirit; when the spirit is harmed, fear arises, leading to physical ailments that manifest in deterioration and a faded complexion, resulting in death during winter.

If the spleen is worried and cannot find relief, it damages the will; when the will is harmed, it causes confusion, resulting in weakened limbs, a faded complexion, and death in spring. When the liver feels sorrow, it harms the soul; when the soul is damaged, it leads to wild forgetfulness and lack of clarity. This lack of clarity causes contraction and tightness in the body, leading to weakened limbs, a faded complexion, and death in autumn.

When the lungs experience endless joy, they harm the ethereal soul; when the soul is harmed, it causes madness, leading to a loss of self-awareness, resulting in dry skin, a faded complexion, and death in summer. When the kidneys are filled with anger and do not cease, they harm the will; when the will is damaged, joy turns into forgetfulness of promises, causing the back to become rigid and the body to lose flexibility, resulting in a faded complexion and death in late summer.

Unresolved fear harms the essence; when the essence is damaged, it leads to bone pain and weakness. Thus, the five organs are responsible for storing essence and must not be harmed. If they are harmed, it leads to a loss of balance, causing deficiency; in deficiency, there is no energy, and without energy, there is death. The "Spiritual Pivot" discusses the illnesses governed by the spirit, will, soul, essence, and consciousness. However, without the influences of cold, heat, shock, or exhaustion, the conclusions can be inferred and broadened.[30p]

怒气所至，为呕血，为飧泄，为煎厥，为薄厥，为阳厥，为胸满胁痛、食则气逆而不下，为喘渴烦心，为消瘅，为肥气，为目暴盲、耳暴闭、筋解发于外，为痈疽。喜气所至，为笑不休，为毛发焦，为内病，为阳气不收，甚则为狂。悲气所至，为阴缩，为筋挛，为肌痹，为脉痿，男为数溲血，女为血崩，为酸鼻辛頞，为目昏，为少气不足以息，为泣则臂麻。恐气所至，为破(月囷)脱肉，为骨酸痿厥，为暴下绿水，为面热肤急，为阴痿，为惧而脱颐。惊气所至，为潮涎，为目瞏，为口呿，为痴癎，为不省人，为僵仆，久则为痛痹。[31p]

When anger arises, it leads to vomiting blood, diarrhea, convulsions, light-headedness, sunken qi, fullness in the chest with pain in the sides, food causes qi to rebel and not descend, shortness of breath and thirst causing distress, consumption of fluids, obesity, sudden blindness, sudden hearing loss, muscles tense and feel released on the outside, and festering sores.

When joy arises, it leads to endless laughter, hair becoming frizzy, internal illness, inability to retain yang qi, and in severe cases, madness.

When sorrow arises, it leads to contraction of the yin, muscle spasms, paralysis of the muscles, weak pulse, in men it causes blood in urine, in women it causes excess menstrual bleeding, sour nasal sensation, blurred vision, insufficient breath support to sigh, and when crying, arm numbness.

When fear arises, it leads to skin peeling off, aching bones and weakness, sudden green diarrhea, heat and urgency in the face, impotence, and fear causing dislocation of the jaw.

When shock arises, it leads to excessive saliva, unfocused eyes, inability to speak, seizures, loss of consciousness, rigidity and collapsing, and if prolonged, it leads to painful numbness.[31p]

劳气所至，为咽噎病，为喘促，为嗽血，为腰痛骨痿，为肺鸣，为高骨坏，为阴痿，为唾血，为冥视，为耳闭，男为少精，女为不月，衰甚则溃溃乎若坏都，汨汨乎不可止。思气所至，为不眠，为嗜卧，为昏瞀，为中痞、三焦闭塞，为咽嗌不利，为胆瘅呕苦，为筋痿，为白淫，为得后与气则快然如衰，为不嗜食，寒气所至为上下所出水液澄彻清冷，下利清白，吐利腥秽，食已不饥，坚痞腹满急痛，症瘕(疒颓)疝，屈伸不便，厥逆禁固。炅气所至，为喘呕吐酸，暴注下迫，转筋，小便浑浊，腹胀大而鼓之有声如鼓，疮疽疡疹，瘤气结核，吐下霍乱，瞀郁肿胀，鼻窒鼽衄，血溢血泄，淋闭，身热恶寒，甚则瞀瘈，目昧不明，耳鸣或聋，躁扰狂越，骂詈惊骇禁栗，如丧神守，气逆冲上，唾腥涌溢，食不下，胕肿疼酸，暴喑暴注，暴病暴死。凡此九者，《内经》有治法，但以五行相胜之理治之。夫怒伤肝，肝属木，怒则气并于肝而脾土受邪，木太过则肝亦自病。[32p]

When the energy is disturbed, it can lead to conditions such as choking, shortness of breath, coughing up blood,腰痛, bone atrophy, lung wheezing, bone decay, impotence, spitting blood, dim vision, ear blockage, reduced male vitality, and irregular menstruation in women. If it becomes severe, it can lead to a collapse akin to a ruined city, flowing uncontrollably. When the mind is disturbed, it can cause insomnia, excessive sleepiness, dizziness, obstruction in the three burning spaces (upper, middle, and lower), throat discomfort, gallbladder stagnation with bitter vomiting, weakness in the muscles, excessive sexual fluid, and when gas becomes stagnant, it can feel light and fleeting. Additionally, it can cause an aversion to food. When cold energy disrupts, it leads to clear and cold bodily fluids being excreted from above and below, diarrhea with clear water, vomiting of foul substances, loss of appetite, and severe abdominal distention with urgent pain and congestion, as well as various lumps, hernias, and difficulty in bending or stretching, with symptoms of cold extremities and rigidity. When heat energy disrupts, it causes shortness of breath, acidic vomiting, immediate pressure below, muscle cramps, cloudy urine, a swollen abdomen that makes sounds like a drum, sores, ulcers, and various skin eruptions, as well as vomiting, diarrhea, confusion, swelling in the nose, bleeding, excessive heat or chills in the body, and in severe cases, disorientation, dim vision, ringing or deafness in the ears, anxiety and madness, exclamations of shock, as if one has lost their mind, with energy in reverse rising up, spitting foul fluids, loss of appetite, painful and swollen areas, sudden onset of serious illness, and death.

All nine of these conditions can be treated as per the principles outlined in the "Inner Canon," specifically by applying the methods of the five elements in a mutually restraining approach. Anger damages the liver which belongs to wood; when one is angry, the energy congregates in the liver, and the spleen, associated with earth, becomes affected; if wood becomes excessive, the liver will also suffer.[32p]

喜伤心，心属火，喜则气并于心而肺金受邪，火太过则心亦自病。悲伤肺，肺属金，悲则气并于肺而肝木受邪，金太过则肺亦自病。恐伤肾，肾属水，恐则气并于肾而心火受邪，水太过，则肾亦自病。思伤脾，脾属土，思则气并于脾而肾水受邪，土太过，则脾亦自病。寒伤形，形属阴。寒胜热则阳受病，寒太过则阴亦自病。炅伤气，气属阳。热胜寒则阴受病，热太过则阳亦自病。凡此七者，更相为治。故悲可以治怒，以怆恻苦楚之言感之；喜可以治悲，以谑浪戏狎之言娱之；恐可以治喜，以迫遽死亡之言怖之；怒可以治思，以污辱欺罔之言触之；思可以治恐，以虑彼志此之言夺之。凡此五者，必诡诈谲怪，无所不至，然后可以动人耳目，易人视听。若胸中无材器之人，亦不能用此五法也。[33p]

Joy harms the heart, while the heart is associated with fire. When joy is excessive, the qi converges in the heart, causing the lungs (metal) to suffer from affliction; if fire is too strong, the heart will also be ill. Grief harms the lungs, which are associated with metal. When grief is excessive, the qi converges in the lungs, causing the liver (wood) to suffer from affliction; if metal is too strong, the lungs will also be ill. Fear harms the kidneys, which are associated with water. When fear is excessive, the qi converges in the kidneys, causing the heart (fire) to suffer from affliction; if water is too strong, the kidneys will also be ill. Thinking harms the spleen, which is associated with earth. When thought is excessive, the qi converges in the spleen, causing the kidneys (water) to suffer from affliction; if earth is too strong, the spleen will also be ill. Cold harms the body, which is associated with yin. When cold overcomes heat, yang suffers illness; if cold is too strong, yin will also be ill. Heat harms the qi, which is associated with yang. When heat overcomes cold, yin suffers illness; if heat is too strong, yang will also be ill.

All of these seven factors affect each other. Therefore, grief can remedy anger by moving it with words of compassion and distress; joy can remedy grief by entertaining it with playful and frivolous words; fear can remedy joy by daunting it with urgent words of impending death; anger can remedy thought by provoking it with words of insult and deceit; thought can remedy fear by removing it with words that consider the intentions of others. All five of these methods must be devious and peculiar, employing whatever means necessary to move people's hearts and eyes, making it easier to influence their sight and hearing. However, if a person lacks the tools and resources within them, they cannot employ these five methods.[33p]

炅可以治寒。寒在外者，以焠针(火矣)熨烙灸，汤而汗之；寒在内者，以热食温剂平之。寒可以治炅。炅在外者，以清房凉榻薄衣，以清剂汗之；炅在内者，以寒饮寒剂平之。惟逸可以治劳，经曰劳者温之，温谓温存而养之。今之医者，以温为温暖之药，差之远矣。岐伯曰：以平为期，亦谓休息之也。惟习可以治惊，经曰惊者平之，平谓平常也。夫惊以其忽然而遇之也，使习见习闻则不惊矣。此九者，《内经》，自有是理，庸工废而不行，今代刘河间治五志，独得言外之意，谓：五志所发，皆从心造，故凡见喜怒悲恐思之证，皆以平心火为主。至于劳者伤于动，动便属阳；惊者骇于心，心便属火。二者亦以平心为主。今之医者不达此旨，遂有寒凉之谤，群聚而噪之，士大夫又从而惑之，公议何时而定耶？[34p]

Jiong can treat cold. For cold outside, use a heated needle (fire) to cauterize and induce sweating; for cold inside, balance it with warm food and warming medicines. Cold can also treat jiong. For jiong outside, use a cool room, a chilly bed, and light clothing to induce sweating with cooling medicines; for jiong inside, balance it with cold drinks and cold medicines. Only rest can treat fatigue, as the classics say, fatigue should be warmed, which means to care for and nurture it. Modern doctors have a far-off understanding, treating warmth as simply a warming medicine. Qi Bo said: to balance is to rest as well. Only habituation can treat fright, as the classics say, fright should be balanced, referring to stability. Fright comes unexpectedly, but if one becomes accustomed to seeing and hearing, one will not be startled. These nine principles are from the "Inner Canon," inherently rational, yet inept craftsmen abandon them. In the present day, Liu Hejian interprets the five emotions, uniquely grasping the deeper meaning, stating that the five emotions arise from the heart; thus, the signs of joy, anger, sorrow, fear, and thought are all centered on balancing heartfire. Furthermore, fatigue is caused by movement, and movement belongs to yang; fright stems from the heart, and the heart belongs to fire. Both of these are also centered on balancing the heart. Modern doctors do not grasp this intention, leading to misunderstandings about coldness, which proliferate noisily. Scholars and officials are confused by it—when will public opinion solidify?[34p]

　　　　医学入门 【明　李梴】

　　　　　情病治法

　　怒伤肝，气上逆，过则呕吐，枳梗二陈汤、绀珠正气天香汤，热者柴陈汤。忧伤肺，其气聚，过则喘促，苏子降气汤、分气紫苏饮。噎膈者，暂用五膈宽中饮。悲伤心胞及肺系，其气急，过则为狂者，枳壳煮散、升阳顺气汤。思伤脾，其气结，过则痞满，退热清气汤、温胆汤、木香化滞汤、木香枳朮丸。此四者，皆令邪气郁结，多见有余之证。又逸则气滞，亦令气结，轻者行动即愈，重者橘皮一物汤。[35p]

Introduction to Medicine
[Ming Dynasty - Li Chan]

Methods for Treating Emotional Illnesses

Anger harms the liver, causing qi to rise and leading to vomiting if excessive. Use the Er Chen Tang with Zhi Ke, or the Gan Zhu Zheng Qi Tian Xiang Tang; if there is heat, use Chai Chen Tang. Worry harms the lungs, causing qi to accumulate and leading to wheezing if excessive. Use Su Zi Jiang Qi Tang or Fen Qi Zi Su Yin. For a throat obstruction, temporarily use the Wu Ge Kuan Zhong Yin. Sadness harms the heart and lung systems, causing qi to become urgent, and if excessive can lead to madness. Use Zhi Ke decocted to disperse, or Sheng Yang Shun Qi Tang. Thoughtfulness harms the spleen, causing qi stagnation and leading to fullness if excessive. Use Tui Re Qing Qi Tang, Wen Dan Tang, Mu Xiang Hua Zhi Tang, or Mu Xiang Zhi Shu Wan. These four conditions all lead to the stagnation of evil qi, commonly presenting as excess symptoms. Furthermore, if there is excess, it can cause qi stagnation as well; if mild, movement can relieve it, if severe, use the Ju Pi Yi Wu Tang.[35p]

　　　　医宗必读 【明　李中梓】

　　　　　恐属四脏

　　经曰：在脏为肾，在志为恐。又云：精气并于肾则恐。盖恐者肾之情志，下章之言他脏者，亦莫不由于肾也。肝藏血，血不足则恐，肝者肾之子也，水强则胆壮，水薄则血虚而为恐矣。胃为恐，胃属土，肾属水，土邪伤水则为恐也。心怵惕思虑则伤神，神伤则恐惧自失。夫心藏神，神伤则心怯，所以恐惧自失，火伤畏水之故。按经文论恐有肾肝心胃四脏之分，而肝胆于肾，乙癸同源者也；胃之于肾，侮所不胜者也；心之于肾，畏其所胜者也。故恐之一证，属肾之本志，而旁及于他脏，治法则有别焉。治肾伤者，宜味厚，枸杞、远志、地黄、山茱萸、茯苓、牛膝、杜仲之属。治肝胆者，宜养阴，枣仁、山茱萸、牡丹皮、白芍药、甘草、龙齿之属。治阳明者，壮其气，四君子汤倍加茯苓。治心君者，镇其神，朱砂、琥珀、金银箔、犀角、龙齿之属。[36p]

Essentials of Medical Tradition 【Ming - Li Zhongzi】

Fear Associated with the Four Organs

The classics say: In the organs, it is the kidneys; in emotions, it is fear. It also states: When essence and qi converge in the kidneys, there is fear. Fear is, therefore, the emotional state associated with the kidneys. The discussion regarding other organs in the following sections also links back to the kidneys. The liver stores blood; when blood is insufficient, there is fear. The liver is the child of the kidneys. When water is abundant, the gallbladder is strong; when water is lacking, blood becomes deficient, causing fear. The stomach is also related to fear—the stomach belongs to earth, while the kidneys belong to water. When earth harms water, fear arises. The heart, when troubled by anxiety and thinking, harms the spirit. When the spirit is harmed, fear and loss of composure follow. The heart houses the spirit; when the spirit is hurt, the heart becomes timid, leading to fear and loss of composure, akin to fire being fearful of water.

In examining the classics, fear is associated with the kidneys, liver, heart, and stomach. The liver and gallbladder are linked to the kidneys, sharing the same source; the stomach in relation to the kidneys is something that cannot be surpassed; and the heart in relation to the kidneys is fearful of being overpowered. Hence, the phenomenon of fear is fundamentally tied to the kidneys, while also involving other organs; thus, treatment methods differ accordingly. For kidney injuries, one should adopt nourishing flavors, using herbs like goji berries, polygala root, rehmannia root, cornelian cherry, poria, achyranthes, and eucommia bark. For liver and gallbladder nourishing, one should focus on nourishing yin with herbs such as sour jujube seed, cornelian cherry, peony root, white peony, licorice, and dragon's teeth. For treating the Yangming system, one needs to boost vitality, using a modified Four Gentlemen Decoction with increased poria. To stabilize the heart, one should calm the spirit with herbs like cinnabar, amber, gold and silver leaf, rhinoceros horn, and dragon's teeth.[36p]

　　　　医门法律 【清　喻昌】

　　　　　心为脏腑之主

　　本神篇曰：心怵惕思虑则伤神，神伤则恐惧自失。邪气脏腑病形篇曰: 忧愁恐惧则伤心。口问篇曰：悲哀忧愁则心动，心动则五脏六腑皆摇。可见心为五脏六腑之大主，而总统魂魄，兼该志意。故忧动于心则肺应，思动于心则脾应，怒动于心则肝应，恐动于心则肾应，此所以五志惟心所使也。设能善养此心，而居处安静，无为惧惧，无为欣欣，婉然从物而不争，与时变化而无我，则志意和，精神定，悔怒不起，魂魄不散，五脏俱宁，邪亦安从奈我何哉？[37p]

Medical Laws of the Physician
By Yu Chang, Qing Dynasty

The Heart as the Master of the Organs

The "Essence of the Heart" says: When the heart is anxious and overthinks, it injures the spirit; if the spirit is harmed, fear and confusion arise. The passage on "Evil Qi and Organ Afflictions" states: Worry and fear injure the heart. The "Inquiry on the Mouth" notes: Sadness and worry disturb the heart, which in turn causes all the five viscera and six bowels to be shaken. It is evident that the heart is the great master of the five viscera and six bowels, presiding over the soul and spirit, and encompassing intention and will. Therefore, when worry arises in the heart, the lungs respond; when thoughts arise in the heart, the spleen responds; when anger arises in the heart, the liver responds; when fear arises in the heart, the kidneys respond. This illustrates how the five emotions are directed by the heart. If one can nurture this heart well, dwell in tranquility, remain untroubled by fear or overly joyful, gracefully adapt to circumstances without contention, and change with time without a strong sense of self, then intention and will are harmonious, the spirit is settled, regret and anger do not arise, the soul remains intact, and the five viscera are at peace. Thus, what can evil do to me?[37p]

　　　　石室秘箓 【清　陈士铎】

　　　　　怒伤肝治法

　　凡人有郁郁不乐，忽然气塞而不能言，苟治之不得法则死矣。夫郁证未有不伤肝者也，伤肝又可伐肝乎？伐肝是愈助其郁，郁且不能解，又何以救死于顷刻哉？方用救肝开郁汤，白芍二两，柴胡、甘草各一钱，白芥子三钱，白朮、茯苓、当归各五钱，陈皮二钱，水煎服。一剂而声出，再剂而神安，三剂而郁气尽解。此方妙在用白芍之多至二两，则直入肝经，以益其匮乏之气，自然血生而火熄；又用白朮、当归健土以生血，柴胡以解郁，甘草以和中，白芥子以消膈膜之痰；又妙在多用茯苓，使郁气与痰涎，尽入于膀胱之中，而消弭于无形也。倘人有郁气不解，奄奄黄瘦，亦急以此方治之，何至变生不测哉！[38p]

Secret Formula of the Stone Chamber
[Qing Dynasty - Chen Shiduo]

Treatment Method for Liver Injury Due to Anger

When a person feels gloomy and unhappy, and suddenly suffers from a blockage of energy that prevents them from speaking, if not treated properly, they may die. Gloom has always inflicted harm on the liver; can one injure the liver further? Injuring the liver only exacerbates the gloom, which cannot be alleviated. How then can one save a life in an instant?

The formula to rescue the liver and open up the gloom consists of:
Two taels of White Peony Root,
One qian each of Bupleurum and Licorice,
Three qians of White Mustard Seed,
Five qians each of Atractylodes, Poria, and Angelica,
Two qians of Dried Tangerine Peel,
Boil with water and take orally.

One dose will restore the voice, the second will calm the spirit, and the third will completely resolve the stagnant energy. The brilliance of this formula lies in the use of a maximum of two taels of White Peony Root, which directly enters the liver channel to replenish its deficient energy, naturally allowing the blood to be generated and the fire to be extinguished. Additionally, the use of Atractylodes and Angelica nourishes the earth to produce blood, Bupleurum alleviates stagnation, Licorice harmonizes the center, and White Mustard Seed dissolves phlegm obstructing the diaphragm. Furthermore, the heavy use of Poria ensures that stagnant energy and phlegm are entirely absorbed into the bladder and dissipated without a trace.

If a person has unresolved stagnation and appears wan and emaciated, they must be treated urgently with this formula, lest they undergo unforeseen transformations![38p]

　　　　　胆怯治法

　　凡人胆怯不敢见人者，少阳胆经虚也。而所以致少阳胆经之虚者，肝木之衰也。而肝木之衰，又因肾水之不足，法当补肾以生肝木。方用熟地一两，山茱萸四钱，芍药、当归、茯神各五钱，柴胡、白芥子、枣仁、肉桂各一钱，水煎服。此方之妙，补肾之中用补肝之品。尤妙再去补心，使心不取给于肝胆之血，则胆之汁有余而怯形可去。又妙用肉桂以入肝，如人得勇往之人，自然顷刻胆壮矣。此治腑实有妙理，人知之乎？[39p]

Treatment for Timidity

When a person is timid and dares not face others, it is due to the deficiency of the lesser yang gallbladder meridian. The cause of this deficiency in the lesser yang gallbladder meridian is the weakness of the liver wood. Furthermore, the weakness of the liver wood results from the insufficient water of the kidneys. The treatment should therefore focus on nourishing the kidneys to promote the growth of the liver wood.

For this, use one ounce of cooked rehmannia, four taels of mountain cornel, five taels each of peony, angelica, and poria, and one tael each of bupleurum, white mustard seed, jujube seeds, and cinnamon. Prepare this as a decoction to take.

The effectiveness of this formula lies in its ability to nourish the kidneys while also replenishing the liver. It is particularly ingenious to omit anything that nourishes the heart, ensuring that the heart does not draw blood from the liver and gallbladder. This way, the bile can become abundant and the timidity can be alleviated. Additionally, using cinnamon to enter the liver is brilliant, as it instills courage, making the timid naturally bold.

This treatment has profound principles. Does anyone know of it?[39p]

　　　　方

　　补心丸 【《千金方》，下同】

Major Settling the Heart Powder treats heart deficiency, fear, palpitations, and anxieties from dreams.
