　　　　针灸

　　《素问》曰：肝虚则目(目巟)(目巟)无所见，耳无所闻，善恐，如人将捕之，取其经厥阴与少阳。　　肾虚则胸中痛，大腹小腹痛，清厥，意不乐，取其经少阴太阳血者。　　阳明令人腰痛不可以顾，顾如有见者，善悲，刺阳明于胻前三痏，上下和之，出血，秋无见血。　　解脉令人腰痛如引带，常如折腰状，善恐，刺解脉在郄中，结络如黍米，刺之血射以黑，见赤血而已。　　飞扬之脉令人腰痛，痛上怫怫然，甚则悲以恐，刺飞扬之脉，在内踝上五寸，少阴之前，与阴维之会。　　人有所堕坠，恶血留内，腹中胀满，不得前后，先饮利药，此上伤厥阴之脉，下伤少阴之络，刺足内踝之下然谷之前血脉出血，刺足跗上动脉；不已，刺三毛上各一痏，见血立已。左刺右，右刺左。善悲惊不乐，刺如右方。　　邪客于足少阴之络，令人嗌痛，不可内食，无故善怒，气上走贲上，刺足下中央之脉各三痏，凡六刺立已。左刺右，右刺左。[52p]

Acupuncture

The "Su Wen" states: When the liver is weak, the eyes can see nothing, and the ears can hear nothing; one feels great fear, as if one were about to be captured. Treat using the channels of the Jueyin and Shaoyang. When the kidneys are weak, there is pain in the chest and pain in the abdomen, both upper and lower; there is a feeling of emptiness, and one is not happy. Treat using the channels of the Shaoyin and Taiyang to access the blood. The Yangming channel causes pain in the lower back, making it impossible to turn; if one turns, it feels as if there is something visible, leading to a feeling of sorrow. Acupuncture on the Yangming channel at three points before the knee and harmonizing above and below will cause bleeding; in autumn, it does not bleed. The Jie Mai channel causes lower back pain as if pulled by a strap, often in a bent-over posture, leading to great fear. Acupuncture on the Jie Mai at the Xie point will cause blood to flow, shooting out like millet; bleeding will show red blood only.

The Feiyang channel causes lower back pain, with a sensation of heaviness that may lead to sorrow and fear. Acupuncture on the Feiyang channel located five "cuns" above the inner ankle, in front of the Shaoyin and where it meets the Yinwei, is beneficial. If someone experiences a fall, with evil blood retained internally, causing abdominal distention and an inability to move forward or backward, one should first drink a laxative. This affects the upper channel of Jueyin and the lower channel of Shaoyin. Acupuncture below the inner ankle in front of the Yangu will cause blood to flow, and acupuncture on the proximal artery of the foot will require several needles; if not effective, needle three points on the upper foot to encourage blood flow, showing blood immediately. Needle on the left for the right side, and on the right for the left. If one is sorrowful, startled, or unhappy, needle as if aiming to the right.

When evil enters the channels of the foot's Shaoyin, it causes throat pain and an inability to eat, alongside unreasonable anger with Qi rising to the upper regions. Needle the central meridian below the foot three times each side, totaling six needle points for immediate relief. Needle on the left for the right side, and on the right for the left.[52p]

　　《灵枢经》曰：胆病者，善太息，口苦呕宿汁，心下淡淡，恐人将捕之，嗌中吤吤然，数唾，在足少阳之本末，亦视其脉之陷下者灸之；其寒热者，取阳陵泉。　　善怒而不欲食，言益小，取足太阴；怒而多言，刺足少阳。　　厥阴为阖，阖折即气绝而喜悲，悲者取之厥阴，视有余不足。　　邪在心则病心痛喜悲，时眩仆，视有余不足而调之其输也。　　厥头痛，头脉痛，心悲喜泣，视头动脉反盛者，刺尽去血，后调足厥阴。[53p]

The "Spiritual Pivot" states: Those suffering from gallbladder illness often sigh deeply, have a bitter taste in the mouth, and may vomit residual juices. They feel a slight discomfort in the heart area, fear being caught by others, and experience a gurgling sensation in the throat with frequent spitting. For issues at the root of the lesser yang, one should also examine the pulse for any sinking sensations and perform moxibustion. For cold and heat, treat at Yanglingquan.

Those who are easily angered and have no desire to eat tend to speak less; treat at the foot of the greater yin. If anger leads to excessive talking, needle the lesser yang on the foot.

The Jueyin relates to closure; if it withdraws, the flow of energy is cut off, leading to feelings of joy and sorrow. For sorrowful feelings, treat the Jueyin while observing any excess or deficiency. If the evil suffers in the heart, it leads to heartache, emotional fluctuations, and periods of dizziness or fainting; assess any excess or deficiency accordingly for treatment.

In cases of head pain and headache pulses, with feelings of sorrow, joy, and tears, treat the overflowing in the head arteries by draining blood, and subsequently adjust the foot at the Jueyin.[53p]

　　黄帝曰：人之哀而泣涕者，何气使然？岐伯曰：心者，五脏六腑之主也。目者，宗脉之所聚也，上液之道也。口鼻者，气之门户也。故悲哀愁忧则心动，心动则五脏六腑皆摇，摇则宗脉感，宗脉感则液道开，液道开故泣涕出焉。液者所以灌精濡空窍者也，故上液之道开则泣，泣不止则液竭，液竭则精不灌，精不灌则目无所见矣。故命曰夺精，补天柱经挟颈。　　《甲乙经》曰：短气心痹，悲怒逆气，怒狂易，鱼际主之。　　心痛善悲，厥逆，悬心如饥之状，心憺憺而惊，大陵及间使主之。　　心憺憺而善惊恐心悲，内关主之。
　　惊善悲不乐，如堕坠，汗不出，面尘黑，病饮不欲食，照海主之。　　《千金方》曰：列缺，主四肢厥，喜笑。　　内庭，主喜频，数欠伸，恶闻人音。　　章门，主四肢懈惰喜怒。[54p]

The Yellow Emperor asked: What causes a person to grieve and shed tears? Qibo replied: The heart is the master of the five viscera and six bowels. The eyes are where the primary vessels converge and are the path for ascending fluids. The mouth and nose are the gateways of breath. Therefore, when sad, grieved, or anxious, the heart is moved; when the heart moves, all the five viscera and six bowels are shaken; when shaken, the primary vessels are affected; when affected, the fluid pathways open; thus, tears flow. The fluids are what nourish and moisten the empty orifices, so when the path for ascending fluids is open, tears flow; if tears flow continuously, the fluids become depleted; when the fluids are depleted, essence cannot be nourished; when essence is not nourished, the eyes can see nothing. Hence it is termed the loss of essence, and the treatment involves supplementing the Tianshu channel along the neck.

The "Classic of Difficulties" states: Shortness of breath and heart block, sadness and anger reversing the qi, sudden impulse of anger, are governed by the fish border (the acupoint).

Heart pain associated with sadness, reversed qi, a feeling of the heart hanging as if hungry, a heart fluttering and startled, is governed by Daling and Jianshi points.

Fluttering and easily startled when sad, the inner pass governs the heart’s sorrow.

Sudden fright brings sadness and discomfort, akin to a fall, with no sweating, the face turns dark; this condition involves a loss of desire for food and drink, governed by the Zhaohai point.

The "Thousand Gold Prescriptions" states: Lieque governs the four limbs' lack of strength and elation.

Neiting governs frequent joy, frequent yawning, and a dislike of hearing others' voices.

Zhangmen governs the lack of energy in the four limbs, joy, and anger.[54p]

　　左手关前寸口阴实者，心实也。若心下有水气，忧恚发之，刺手心主治阴。　　通里，主卒痛烦心，心中懊憹，数欠频伸，心下悸，悲恐。　　漏谷，主肠鸣强欠，心悲气逆，腹(月真)满急。　　天井、神道、心腧，主悲愁恍惚，悲伤不乐。　　间使，主善悲惊狂，面赤目黄，喑不能言。　　少冲，主太息烦满，少气悲惊。
　　行间，主心痛数惊，心悲不乐。
　　商丘，主心下有寒痛；又主脾虚，令人病不乐，好太息。　　太冲，主羸瘦恐惧，气不足，腹中悒悒。　　支正、鱼际、合谷、少海、曲池、腕骨，主狂言惊恐。　　然谷、阳陵泉，主心中怵惕，恐如人将捕之状。　　少府，主数噫恐悸，气不足。
　　左手关上阳绝者，无胆脉也。苦膝疼，口中苦，眯目善畏，如见鬼，多惊少力，刺足厥阴治阴，在足大指间，或刺三毛中。[55p]

The left hand's Guān (关) at the inch mark indicates a deficiency in the heart. If there is moisture in the heart, worries and anger manifest as pain in the palm, which governs the yin.

The Tōng lǐ (通里) point governs sudden pain and distress in the heart, feelings of regret, frequent sighing, palpitations, and fearfulness.

The Lòu gǔ (漏谷) point governs strong rumbling in the intestines, sorrowful emotions, and stagnation in the abdomen.

The Tiān jǐng (天井), Shén dào (神道), and Xīn zhù (心腧) points govern anxiety and feelings of sadness, resulting in an unhappy disposition.

The Jiàn shǐ (间使) point governs excessive sorrow, fright, and delirium, resulting in a flushed face, yellowish eyes, and muteness.

The Shào chōng (少冲) point governs deep sighing, restlessness, and feelings of fright.

The Xíng jiān (行间) point governs heart pain and sudden fears, leading to a dispirited heart.

The Shāng qiū (商丘) point indicates cold pain in the heart, and also signifies spleen deficiency, which causes unhappiness and frequent sighing.

The Tài chōng (太冲) point indicates emaciation and fear, insufficient energy, and anxiety in the abdomen.

The Zhī zhèng (支正), Yú jì (鱼际), Hé gǔ (合谷), Shào hǎi (少海), Qū qū (曲池), and Wàn gǔ (腕骨) points govern excessive talk and terror.

The Rán gǔ (然谷) and Yáng líng quán (阳陵泉) points indicate a state of dread and vigilance, akin to being hunted.

The Shào fǔ (少府) point governs repeated sighs, fear, palpitations, and insufficient energy.

Regarding the left hand's Guān (关) at the upper yang, it signifies an absence of the gallbladder pulse. This condition includes symptoms such as knee pain, a bitter taste in the mouth, squinting, and a propensity to fear, akin to witnessing a ghost, resulting in frequent fright and diminished strength, treated by puncturing the foot's Jue Yin point, located between the big toe or possibly at the third toe.[55p]

　　　　医案

　　《儒门事亲》曰：戴人之次子自出妻后，体日瘦，语如瓮中出，此病在中也。常捻第三指失笑，此心火也。约半载，日饮冰雪，更服凉剂。戴人曰：恶雪则愈矣。其妻惧太寒，戴人曰：吾用药如鼓之应桴，汝亲也，尚恶凉药，宜乎世之谤我也。至七月，厌冰不饮，病日解矣。
　　一人因喜乐之极而病者，庄先生切其脉，为之失声，佯日：吾取药去。数日更不来，病者悲泣，辞其亲友曰：吾不久矣。庄知其将愈慰之。诘其故，庄引《素问》曰：惧胜喜。
　　戴人路经古亳，逢一妇，病喜笑不止，已半年矣。众医皆无术矣。戴人曰：此易治也。以沧盐成块者二两，用火烧令通赤，放冷研细，以河水一大碗，同煎至三五沸，放温，分三次啜之，以钗探于咽中，吐出热痰五升；次服大剂黄连解毒汤，不数日而笑定矣。《内经》曰：神有余则笑不休。此所谓神者，心火是也。火得风而成焰，故笑之象也。五行之中，惟火有笑矣。[56p]

Medical Case Reports

The "Rumen Shiqin" states: Mr. Dai's younger son, after taking a wife, became increasingly thin and spoke as if from within a jar. This illness is internal. He often twirled his third finger and lost his smile; this indicated heart fire. After about half a year, he drank ice and snow daily and took cool medicines. Mr. Dai said: "Avoid the cold, and you will get better." His wife feared it was too cold, and Mr. Dai replied: "I use medicine as one would respond to a drum with a clapper; you, my kin, still dislike cool medicine, thus it is no wonder the world slanders me." By July, he had grown tired of ice and no longer drank it, and his illness gradually diminished.

A certain person fell ill from excessive joy. Mr. Zhuang felt his pulse and rendered him voiceless, pretending to say: "I will fetch medicine now." A few days passed without his return, and the patient wept, bidding farewell to friends and family, saying: "I have not long to live." Mr. Zhuang knew he would recover and comforted him. When inquired, Mr. Zhuang referred to the "Suwen," stating: "Fear overcomes joy."

Mr. Dai, traveling through ancient Bo, encountered a woman who laughed incessantly due to her illness for over half a year. All physicians were at a loss. Mr. Dai said: "This is easy to treat." He took two taels of salt blocks, heated them until red, cooled them down, and ground them finely. He then used a large bowl of river water to boil it until it bubbled three to five times. After it cooled, he administered it in three doses and probed her throat with a hairpin, causing her to expel five liters of hot phlegm. Next, he prescribed a large dose of Huanglian detoxifying decoction, and within a few days, her laughter settled. The "Neijing" states: "When the spirit is excessive, laughter does not cease." This so-called spirit refers to heart fire. When fire receives wind, it forms flames, hence the symbol of laughter. Among the five elements, only fire is associated with laughter.[56p]

　　一富家妇人，伤思虑过甚，二年不寐，无药可疗，其夫求戴人治之。戴人曰：两手脉俱缓，此脾受病，脾主思故也。乃与其夫议，以怒而激之，多取其财，饮酒数日，不处一法而去。其人大怒，汗出，是夜困眠，如此者八九日不寤，自是而进食，脉得其平。
　　洛阳孙伯英因诬狱，妻子被系，逃于故人家，是夜，觉胃胁痛，托故人求药。故人曰：有名医张戴人适在焉，当与公同往。时戴人宿酒未醒，强呼之。故人曰：吾有一亲人病欲求诊。戴人隔窗望见伯英曰：此公伏大惊恐。故人曰：何以知之？戴人曰：面青脱色，胆受怖也。后会赦乃出，方告戴人。
　　霍秀才之子年十二岁，睾丸一旁肿膇，戴人见之曰：此因惊恐得之。惊之为病，上行则为呕血，下则肾伤而为水肿。以琥珀通经散一泻而消散。[57p]

A wealthy woman became overly distressed, unable to sleep for two years, with no medicine to cure her. Her husband sought help from a physician named Dai. Dai examined her and said: "Both pulse points are weak; this is a disorder of the spleen, which governs thought." He advised her husband to provoke her with anger to draw out her emotions, took a great deal of their wealth, drank for several days, and left without providing any treatment. The woman became very angry, perspired, and that night finally fell into a deep sleep. This continued for eight or nine days without waking, after which she began eating again and her pulse returned to normal.

In Luoyang, Sun Boying was wrongfully imprisoned, and his wife and children were also detained. He escaped to a friend's house and that night felt pain in his stomach and side, asking his friend for medicine. The friend replied: "There is a famous doctor, Zhang Dai, nearby; I will go with you to see him." At that time, Dai was still recovering from drinking. The friend urgently called him. Dai, seeing through the window that it was Boying, said: "This person is overtaken by great fear." The friend asked, "How do you know this?" Dai replied: "His face is pale, drained of color; his gallbladder is stricken with fear." After receiving a pardon, Boying went to inform Dai.

Huo Xiucai's twelve-year-old son had swelling on one side of his testicles. Dai examined him and said: "This is caused by fear. When fear manifests as illness, it can lead to vomiting blood if it moves upwards, or cause kidney damage and water retention if it moves downwards." He administered Amber Decoction to help dispel the condition.[57p]

　　《丹溪心法》曰：一妇十九岁，气实多怒，一日，忽大叫而欲厥，盖痰闭于上，火起于下而上冲。始用香附五钱，生甘草三钱，川芎七钱，童便姜汁煎服；又用青黛人中白香附末为丸，稍愈不除；后用大吐乃安。吐后，用导痰汤加姜炒黄连、香附、生姜，煎下龙荟丸而愈。
　　一女许婚后，夫经商二年不归，因不食，困卧如痴，无他病，竟日向壁而卧。其父迎丹溪翁治之，告以故。翁脉毕，谓其父曰：此思则气结也。药难独治，得喜可解。不然，令其怒。于是掌其面，诬以外情，果大怒而号泣者三时。令解之，即求食矣。所以然者，悲则气消，怒则胜思故也。翁谓其父曰：病虽瘥，得喜方已。乃谕以夫回。既而果然，疾亦不举。
　　一妇病不知，稍苏即号叫数四而复昏，丹溪翁诊之，肝脉弦数而且滑，曰：此怒心所为，盖得之怒而强酒也。诘之，则不得于夫，每遇夜自酌解其怀。翁治以消痰降火之剂，而加香附以散肝分之郁，立愈。[58p]

The "Danxi Heart Method" states: A woman, nineteen years old, with an excess of anger, suddenly yelled out one day and nearly fainted. This was due to phlegm obstructing above and fire rising from below. Initially, she was treated with five qian of xiangfu, three qian of sheng gancao, and seven qian of chuanchong, decocted with the urine of a child and ginger juice; she also took a pill made of qingdai and white xiangfu powder, which provided slight relief but did not eliminate the problem. Later, a thorough vomiting was performed and then she stabilized. After the vomiting, a phlegm-dissolving decoction with stir-fried huanglian, xiangfu, and ginger was given, and the Longhui pill was decocted down, leading to her recovery.

A girl, engaged to be married, had her husband away for business for two years without returning; she stopped eating and lay in a stupor, having no other ailments, choosing to lie facing the wall all day. Her father sought the help of Elder Danxi, who diagnosed the situation. After feeling her pulse, the elder stated, "This is due to repressed feelings leading to stagnation of qi. Medicine alone cannot resolve this; she needs joy to relieve it. Otherwise, it will lead to anger." He then slapped her face, falsely accusing her of infidelity until she became extremely angry and cried out three times. Upon being calmed down, she immediately asked for food. The reason is that sadness depletes qi whereas anger overcomes repressed feelings. The elder told her father, "Although her illness may seem cured, only happiness can truly resolve it." He then advised that the husband should return. Eventually, this proved effective, and the illness did not recur.

Another woman fell ill without understanding the cause, and when she slightly regained consciousness, she yelled several times before fainting again. Elder Danxi diagnosed her, finding her liver pulse tense, rapid, and slippery, stating, "This is caused by anger; she must have been angered and then consumed strong liquor." Upon inquiry, it was revealed that she would drink whenever her husband was not around to soothe her feelings. The elder treated her with a formula to dispel phlegm and lower the fire, adding xiangfu to disperse the liver's stagnation, which led to her immediate recovery.[58p]

　　东阳吴子方年五十，形肥味厚，且多忧怒，脉常沉濇，自春来得痰气病，医认为虚寒，率与燥热香窜之剂，至四月间，两足弱，气上冲，饮食减。予曰：此热郁而脾虚，痿厥之证作矣。形肥而脉沉，未是死证，但热邪太盛，当此火旺，实难求生。且与竹沥下白朮膏，尽二斤，气降食进，一月后大汗而死。
　　一女子年逾笄，性躁味厚，暑月因大怒而呃作，每作则举身跳动，神昏不知人，问之，乃知暴病，视其形气俱实，遂以人参芦煎汤，饮一碗，大吐顽痰数碗，大汗昏睡一日而安。人参入手太阴，补阳中之阴者也，芦则反尔大泻太阴之阳。女子暴怒气上，肝主怒，肝主气，经曰怒则气逆，气因怒逆，肝木乘火侮肺，故呃大作而神昏。参芦喜吐，痰尽气降而火衰，金气复位，胃气得和而解。麻黄发汗，节能止汗。谷属金，糠之性热；麦属阳，麸之性凉。先儒谓物物具太极，学者其可不触类而长，引而伸之乎？[59p]

A man from Dongyang, Wu Zifang, was fifty years old, stocky and heavy-set, prone to worries and anger. His pulse was consistently deep and sludgy. Since spring, he suffered from phlegm-qi illness, and the physician deemed it a deficiency of cold, thus usually prescribing warming and aromatic dispersing medicines. By April, his legs became weak, qi surged upwards, and his appetite diminished. I said: this is caused by stagnant heat and a deficient spleen, resulting in symptoms of atrophy and coldness. Although he is corpulent and has a deep pulse, this is not a fatal sign. However, the heat evil is too intense; during this fire's peak, it is really difficult to seek recovery. I prescribed bamboo sap with white atractylodes paste, totaling two pounds. His qi descended and appetite improved, but a month later he broke into a great sweat and died.

A woman over the age of fifteen was energetic and thick in physique. During the hot months, due to a fit of rage, she experienced hiccups, which caused her to jump and move her entire body, becoming dazed and unaware of her surroundings. Upon inquiry, it was discovered she had a sudden illness. Observing her condition, both her form and qi were strong, so I prescribed a decoction of ginseng and reed. After drinking a bowl, she expelled several bowls of stubborn phlegm, broke out in a large sweat, and fell into a deep sleep for a day before recovering. Ginseng enters the hand taiyin channel, nourishing the yin within the yang, while reed greatly drains the yang of the taiyin. The woman, consumed by anger, had qi rising; the liver governs anger. The texts say that anger causes qi to rebel; due to anger, the qi reverses, and the wood of the liver overcomes the fire, oppressing the lungs, hence the severe hiccups and stupor. Ginseng and reed are good for supporting expulsion; with phlegm expelled and qi descending, the fire diminishes, the metal qi restores to its place, and the stomach's qi harmonizes, leading to resolution. Ephedra induces sweating, while also moderating excessive perspiration. Grains belong to metal; the nature of bran is hot. Wheat belongs to yang; the nature of chaff is cool. The ancients said everything possesses the ultimate principle (taiji). Shouldn't scholars engage in a comparative study and broaden their understanding from this?[59p]

　　周本心年六十岁，形气俱实，因大恐，正月间染病，心不自安，如人将捕之状，夜卧亦不安，两耳后亦觉火光炎上，食饮虽进而不知味，口干而不欲食，以人参、白朮、当归身为君，陈皮为佐，加盐炒黄蘗、炙元参各少许，煎服自愈，月余而安。
　　《医学纲目》曰：乡里有一妇人，数次无故悲泣不止，或谓有祟，祈禳请祷备至，终不应。予忽忆《金匮》有一证云：妇人脏燥悲伤欲哭，象如神灵，数欠伸者，宜甘麦大枣汤。予急令治药，尽剂而愈。古人识病制方，种种绝妙如此。[60p]

Zhou Benxin was sixty years old, in good health, but became greatly frightened. In the first month, he fell ill, unable to find peace, feeling as if he were being hunted. He could not sleep well at night, and felt a burning sensation at the back of his ears. Although he ate and drank, he could not taste anything, his mouth was dry, and he had no desire to eat. Using ginseng, white atractylodes, and angelica as the main ingredients, with tangerine peel as an adjunct, he added a little salt, stir-fried yellow gentian, and roasted ginseng, then boiled the mixture, which cured him. After a month, he found peace.

The "Treatise on Medicine" states: In the village, there was a woman who wept endlessly for no reason. Some said she was afflicted by a spirit. Despite prayers and rituals, there was no response. I suddenly remembered a passage from the "Classic of the Golden Coffer" that mentioned: when a woman's internal organs are dry and she feels sorrowful, wanting to cry, resembling the behavior of spirits, if she often stretches and yawns, she should take a decoction of sweet wheat and jujubes. I urgently instructed the preparation of the medicine, and upon taking the full dose, she recovered. The ancients had profound insight into diseases and devised remedies in such remarkable ways.[60p]

　　《薛己医案》曰：一妇人元气素弱，痰气时作，或咽间不利，或胸痞等证，余以为郁结伤脾，用加味归脾汤治之而愈。后遇恚怒，前证仍作，惑于众言，以为痰饮，妄用祛痰之剂，吐泻数次，变诸异证，口禁不醒。余以为脾胃复伤，日用六君子一剂，米饮浓煎，常服匙许，至四日渐进粥食，乃服前药，间以归脾汤，喜其善调养，两月余，诸证悉愈。
　　一妇人因怒患痰厥而苏，左手臂不能伸，手指麻木，口喎眼斜，痰气上攻，两腿骨热，或骨中酸痛，服乌药顺气散之类，诸证益甚，不时昏愦，更加内热晡热。余以为肝经血虚，内热生风，前药复耗肝血，虚火炽盛而益甚也。先以柴胡栀子散，调养肝经气血，数日后，用八珍汤加钓藤钩散，诸证稍愈。又用加减八味丸料，少加酒炒黄蘗、知母黑色者，数剂诸证顿退。乃服八珍汤、柴胡栀子散，半载而痊。后劳役即有复作之意，服柴胡栀子散随安。[61p]

"The Medical Cases of Xue Ji" states: A woman with weak vital energy often experienced phlegm and qi issues, sometimes feeling discomfort in her throat or chest oppression. I believed this was due to stagnation harming the spleen, so I treated her with a modified Gui Pi Decoction, and she recovered. Later, she encountered anger, and her previous symptoms reappeared. Confused by others' opinions, she assumed it was phlegm and wrongly used expectorants, causing repeated vomiting and diarrhea, leading to various new symptoms and a stupor. I thought her spleen and stomach were injured again, so I prescribed Liu Jun Zi Tang daily, made a strong rice drink for her to take by the spoonful. After four days, she gradually progressed to eating porridge, then took the previous medicine, alternating with Gui Pi Decoction. Pleased with its nourishing effects, after more than two months, all symptoms disappeared.

Another woman suffered from phlegm syncope due to anger, unable to stretch her left arm, with numb fingers, and drooping mouth and eyes. Her phlegm and qi surged upward, her legs felt hot, and she experienced bone pain. She took Wuyao Shunqi San and similar remedies, but her symptoms worsened, often feeling dizzy, with increased internal heat. I believed this was due to blood deficiency in the liver meridian, causing internal heat to generate wind, while the previous medicines further depleted liver blood, worsening the excessive fire. I first used Chai Hu Zhi Zhi San to nourish the qi and blood of the liver meridian. After several days, I employed Ba Zhen Tang with added Diao Teng Gou San, and her symptoms slightly improved. I then used the modified Ba Wei Wan, adding a small amount of wine-fried Huang Lian and Zhi Mu (black variety), and after several doses her symptoms retreated significantly. Finally, I continued using Ba Zhen Tang and Chai Hu Zhi Zhi San, and after half a year, she was healed. However, after labor, she felt a recurrence approaching, so I advised her to take Chai Hu Zhi Zhi San as needed."[61p]

　　《医方考》曰：按《闻见录》云：州监军病悲思，其子迎赫允治之，允告其子曰：法当甚悸即愈。时通守李宋卿御史严甚，监军内所畏也。允与其子请于宋卿一造，问责其过失。监军惶怖汗出，疾乃愈。盖思则气结，惊怖则气浮，浮则气不结矣。此亦以情相胜也。
　　赵知则，太原人，因喜成疾，巢氏医脉之，为之惊异，出取药，竟不与之。数日，赵悲哭辞家人曰：处世不久矣。巢知其将愈，使人慰之。诘其故，引《素问》恐胜喜以对，可谓得玄关者也。[62p]

The "Examination of Medical Formulas" states: According to the "Records of Observations," there was a military governor who fell ill due to sorrow. His son sought the help of He Yuyin for treatment. Yuyin told the son, "The method must be applied when his fear is intense, and then he will recover." At that time, the overseeing official, Li Songqing, was extremely severe, and the military governor was greatly intimidated by him. Yuyin and his son went to request an audience with Songqing to discuss the governor's errors. The military governor became anxious and broke into a sweat, which led to his eventual recovery. It is evident that when one is troubled, the energy gets trapped; when frightened, the energy becomes unsettled, and when unsettled, the energy cannot be contained. This illustrates the emotional influence on physical health.

Zhao Zhizhe, a person from Taiyuan, developed a disorder due to excessive joy, which astonished the physicians of the Chao clan. They went to fetch medicine but ultimately did not provide any. A few days later, Zhao mournfully told his family, "My time in this world is short." Chao, knowing he would recover, sent someone to comfort him. When questioned about the reason for his condition, he referenced the "Suwen," suggesting that fear could surpass joy in response, showing a deep understanding of the underlying principles.[62p]

　　韩丞相疾，天方不雨，更十医罔效，左友信最后至，脉已，则以指计甲子曰：某日当雨。竟出。韩疑曰：岂为吾疾不可为耶？何言雨而不及药我也？既而其夕果雨，韩喜，起而行乎庭，达旦，疾若脱去。乃召左至而问之。对曰：公相之疾，以忧得之，私计公相忠且仁，方今久旱，必为民忧，以旱为忧，必以雨而瘳，理固宜然，何待药而愈耶？此亦《素问》喜胜忧也。
　　一县差拿犯人，以铁索项所犯至县，行至中途，其犯投河而死，犯家告差人索骗威逼至死，即能脱罪，未免破财，忧愤成病，如醉如痴，谬言妄语，无复知识。其主延戴念仁视之，戴云：此以费财而病，必以得财而愈。乃命作三锡锭如银状，预置于泥沟之中，候其至时，诈以锁钥误堕其中，命探之，乃出三锡锭。主曰：银也，吾不用此弗义之财，悉以与汝。其差握视不置，病遂日愈。此亦喜胜忧也。[63p]

The Prime Minister Han fell ill, and when the sky showed no sign of rain, ten doctors were of no help. At last, Zuo Youxin arrived, took his pulse, and using his fingers calculated the heavenly stems and earthly branches, declaring: "It will rain on such and such a day." He then left. Han doubted, wondering if his illness was such that he could not be cured. Why speak of rain when medication had not worked for me? That evening, it indeed rained, and Han was overjoyed, rising to walk in the courtyard until dawn, feeling as if his illness had vanished. He summoned Zuo and asked him. Zuo replied: "Your illness was caused by worry. You have been thinking of your loyalty and kindness towards the people, and during this prolonged drought, it is understandable to be anxious for them. To worry about the drought means you also hope for rain to cure it. Thus, it is only natural, so why wait for medicine to be healed? This is also what the 'Suwen' says: joy overcomes worry."

In a certain county, a dispatcher caught a criminal and brought him to the county, but midway, the criminal jumped into the river and died. The criminal's family accused the dispatcher of coercing the man to death through threats. The dispatcher might escape punishment but at the cost of his wealth. Overwhelmed with anger and grief, he fell ill, his mind drifting as if he were drunk, speaking nonsense and losing his senses. The local magistrate, Yan Dai, looked upon him with compassion, and Yan remarked: "This illness has resulted from financial loss and will surely be cured by financial gain." He then ordered three ingots of tin to be made to resemble silver and placed them in a mud ditch, waiting for the right moment. He tricked the dispatcher into mistakenly dropping the keys into the ditch and commanded him to retrieve them, only to bring out the three tin ingots. The magistrate declared: "This is silver, but I will not use this ill-gotten wealth; it must all be given to you." The dispatcher held it but could not part with it, and gradually, the illness diminished. This too is the principle that joy overcomes worry.[63p]

　　一女子母甚是相爱，既嫁而母死，遂思念不已，精神短少，厌厌嗜卧，诸药不应。其夫延韩世良治之。韩曰：此病得之于思，药不易愈，当以术治之。乃贿一巫妇，授以秘语。一日，夫谓妻曰：汝之念母如此，不识彼在地下，亦念汝否？吾当他往，汝盍求巫妇卜之。妻欣诺，遂召巫至，焚香礼拜而母灵降矣。一言一默，宛然其母之生前也。女遂大泣。母叱之曰：勿泣！汝之生命克我，我遂早死，我之死，皆汝之故。今在阴司欲报汝雠，汝病厌厌，实我所为，我生则与尔母子，死则与尔寇雠矣。言讫，女改容大怒，诟之曰：我因母病，母反我害，我何乐而思之？自是而病愈矣。此亦以情疗之也。[64p]

A woman was very close to her mother; after marrying, her mother passed away, and she could not stop longing for her. Her spirit diminished, and she fell into a lethargy, rejecting all medicines. Her husband called upon Han Shiliang to treat her. Han said, "This illness arises from longing; it is not easily cured by medicine but should be treated with skill." He then bribed a witch woman and taught her some secret words. One day, the husband said to his wife, "Your longing for your mother is such that you do not know if she remembers you in the ground as well. I will go somewhere else; why don't you ask the witch woman to divine?" The wife gladly agreed and summoned the witch. After burning incense and paying respects, her mother’s spirit appeared. In every word and silence, she seemed just like she was in life. The daughter wept greatly. The mother reprimanded her, saying, "Do not weep! Your life has caused my death; I died early because of you. My death is all your fault. Now in the underworld, I desire to take revenge on you, and your illness is indeed due to me. When I was alive, I was with you as mother and child; now that I am dead, I am your enemy." After speaking, the daughter’s expression shifted to great anger, and she scolded, "I am ill because of my mother, yet my mother wishes me harm. What joy is there in thinking of her?" From that moment on, her illness was cured. This was also a healing through emotion.[64p]

　　谭植素谨言，为韶州佐，一日，会堂属官，筵中有萝卜颇大，众羡之。谭曰：尚有大如人者。众皆笑以为无。谭悔恨自咎曰：人不见如是大者，而吾以是语之，宜其以吾言为妄且笑也。因而忧愤，连日不能食。其子煌读书达事，思父素不轻言，因愧赧成疾，必实所言，始可疗病。遂遣人至家，取萝卜如人大者，至官所，复会堂属，强父扶疾而陪。酒至数巡，以车载至席前。众皆惊讶，其父大喜，厥旦疾愈，此亦《素问》喜胜忧也。[65p]

Tan Zhi Su was a cautious speaker and served as an assistant in Shaozhou. One day, while at a banquet with his officials, there was a particularly large radish that drew everyone's admiration. Tan said, "There are radishes as large as a person." The crowd laughed, thinking his claim was unbelievable. Tan felt regret and blamed himself, saying, "Since people cannot see such a large one, they are right to dismiss my words as nonsense and laugh." As a result, he became worried and upset, unable to eat for several days. His son, Huang, who was well-read and knowledgeable about matters, remembered how his father rarely spoke lightly. Feeling ashamed, he fell ill and thought that his father's words must be genuine for him to be healed. He then sent someone to fetch a radish as large as a person and brought it to the official residence, insisting his father, who was unwell, accompany him. When the wine flowed and the radish was presented at the banquet, everyone was astonished, and his father was very happy. The next morning, his illness was cured. This is also reminiscent of the teaching in "Suwen" about joy overcoming sorrow.[65p]

　　《寓意草》曰：吴添官生母，时多暴怒，以致经行复止，入秋以来，渐觉气逆上厥，如畏舟船之状，动辄运去，久卧于床。时若天翻地覆，不能强起，百般医治不效，因用人参三五分，略宁片刻，最后增至五钱一剂，日费数金，意图旦夕苟安，以视稚子究竟。家产尽废，病转凶危，大热引饮，脑间有如刀劈，食少泻多，已治木，无他望矣。闻余返娄延诊过，许以可救，因委命以听焉。余以怒甚则血菀于上，而气不返于下者，名曰厥巅疾。厥者逆也，巅者高也。气与血俱逆于高巅，故动辄眩运也。又以上盛下虚者，过在少阳。少阳者，足少阳胆也。[66p]

The "Yuyi Cao" states: Wu Tian's mother often experienced violent anger, which caused her menstrual cycle to stop. Since autumn, she gradually felt an upward reversal of Qi, as if fearing the rocking of a boat, and would immediately feel unwell, spending long periods lying in bed. It was as if the world was turned upside down, making it impossible for her to rise. Various medical treatments proved ineffective, so she began using three to five fen of ginseng, which offered slight relief for a moment. Eventually, she increased the dosage to five qian per dose, spending several golden coins daily, hoping for a quick stabilization to care for her young child. Her family's wealth was exhausted, her illness grew more critical, and she experienced intense thirst and pain, as if her head were being sliced by a knife. She ate little and had frequent diarrhea; she had treated her liver, but there were no other hopes left. Upon hearing that I returned to Lou Yan for a diagnosis, she entrusted me with her care, believing that I could save her. I explained that extreme anger causes blood to stagnate upwards, preventing Qi from descending; this is called the "Reversal of Qi at the Vertex." The term "reversal" signifies an upward direction, while "vertex" denotes a high point. When both Qi and blood surge upwards, dizziness and disturbances occur. Furthermore, with excess above and deficiency below, the cause lies in the lesser Yang. The lesser Yang pertains to the Gallbladder meridian of the foot.[66p]

胆之穴皆络于脑，郁怒之火，上攻于脑，得补而炽，其痛如劈，同为厥巅之疾也。风火相煽，故振摇而热；木土相凌，故艰食而多泻也。于是会《内经》铁落镇坠之意，以代赭石、龙胆草、芦荟、黄连之属，降其上逆之气；以蜀漆、丹皮、赤芍之属，行其上脘之血；以牡蛎、龙骨、五味之属，敛其浮游之神。最要在每剂药中，加入生猪胆汁二枚，盖以少阳热炽，胆汁必干，亟以同类之物济之，资其持危扶颠之用。病者药一入口，便若神返其舍，忘其苦口，连进十数剂，服猪胆二十余枚，热退身凉，饮食有加，便泻自止，始能起床，行动数步。然尚觉身轻如叶，不能久支。仆恐药味太苦，不宜多服，减去猪胆及芦龙等药，加入当归一钱人参三分，姜枣为引，平调数日而全愈。
[67p]

The gallbladder points are all connected to the brain. When the fire of pent-up anger attacks upwards to the brain and receives a supplement, it intensifies, causing pain akin to splitting, which is the same condition as vertigo. The wind and fire stir each other, hence causing trembling and heat; the wood and earth conflict, leading to difficulty in eating and excessive diarrhea.

Thus, the intention from the Inner Canon about the "iron ball sinking" is employed, substituting substances like cinnabar, gentian, aloe, and rhubarb to counteract the rebellious qi. With substances such as Chinese lacquer, peony root, and red peony to circulate the blood in the upper stomach; and with oyster shell, dragon bone, and five flavors to stabilize the wandering spirit.

It is crucial to add two doses of fresh pig bile into each prescription, as the heat of the lesser yang will surely dry the bile. Immediately, similar substances need to be supplemented to support and stabilize the patient. When the patient takes one dose of medicine, it is as if their spirit returns to its place, forgetting the bitter taste, and they can take ten or more doses, consuming over twenty doses of pig bile. The heat subsides, the body cools, appetite increases, diarrhea halts, and they can finally rise and move a few steps. However, they still feel light as a leaf and cannot endure for long.

I feared that the bitterness of the medicine might be excessive and not suitable for prolonged use, so I reduced the pig bile and the other herbs, adding one qian of angelica and three fen of ginseng, using ginger and jujube as a guide, adjusting the formula over several days until they were completely cured.[67p]
